from time to time approved by the Town Council.
   B.   Appointment: No person shall be accepted to the position of volunteer
EMT until he has taken a training course prescribed by the Wyoming Emergency
Service Regulations, and passed an examination indicating adequate knowledge of
the matters taught in the course. Such test shall be prescribed by the State
Emergency Service Office, and matters covered shall include methods of
emergency treatment, operation of equipment, first aid, and such other relevant
items as shall be directed by the State Wyoming Emergency Service Department.
The case of any individual who has prior experience as an EMT on a volunteer
ambulance service or on a full time emergency medical service, the State may
waive any part of the course.
   C.   In Service Training Required: Each volunteer EMT shall take regular
training at least once each month, on the subjects prescribed and in the manner
prescribed by the State Emergency Service regulations. The Captain shall
require a minimum number of hours of training each month for each member as
prescribed by the State regulations. The minimum number of hours shall be the
amount required to learn new techniques and to continue to maintain skills
under old techniques.
   D.   Volunteer Emergency Medical Technicians: Each volunteer EMT shall
receive a nominal fee per assignment basis. Such nominal fee shall be assigned
by the Ambulance Service Board voted on by the members of an annual basis,
subject to the approval of the Town Council.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-5: LIST OF MEMBERS:
The Captain of the ambulance service shall maintain in the Office of the Town
Clerk an accurate list of the members of the service and shall report promptly
any additions or withdrawals from the membership and shall include an updated
copy of every volunteer EMT’s driver’s license, certificate of training, and
current CPR training at every January Town Council meeting.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-6: DUTIES OF OFFICERS AND MEMBERS:
It shall be the duty of every officer and member of the service to obey without
question the orders of his superior officers at all times while in the
emergency medical service station and in going and returning from emergencies.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-7: POLICE AUTHORITY AND RIGHT OF ENTRY:
The Captain of the ambulance service and members acting under his orders shall
have full and complete police powers and authority within the emergency medical
station, at emergencies and proceeding to and returning from them in all
matters pertaining to the ambulance service. The Captain or other officer in
charge shall have authority to prescribe limits within which no person shall be
admitted except by order of the officer. While actually attendant at an
emergency, the Police Captain and his deputy and all other law enforcement
officers of the Town shall be under the orders of the Captain or other officer
of the department in charge of the emergency. Such law enforcement officers
shall cooperate with the medical officer in charge of the enforcement of the
provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-8: EVACUATION:
For the purpose of protecting persons or property, the Captain or other office
of the service in charge of the medical emergency shall have authority to order
the evacuation of any building or premises to promote safety for the public.
5-3-9: RECORDS, REPORTS AND INSPECTIONS:
   A.   Inventory: The Captain of the ambulance service, immediately after
assuming office and annually thereafter, shall make an inventory of all
property owned by the service or in its charge, noting the condition of each
article. The inventory shall be submitted to the Mayor and Town Council at the
regular meeting of the Council last occurring before the meeting in which the
Town Council annually considers and enacts the appropriation of funds to defray
expenses of the Town for the fiscal year. The Captain shall accompany the
inventory of equipment with a list of recommendations for the purchase of
additional equipment, and repairs to existing equipment deemed necessary, and
any other recommendations desired to submit affecting the service.
   B.   Inspections: The Captain shall inspect or cause to be inspected by
members of the department, at least monthly, and more often if necessary, all
ambulances and equipment. Those needing attention will be reported at the next
regular meeting of the Town Council, or as soon as possible if the need is
immediate.
   C.   Reporting Loss Or Damage: Loss of or damage to equipment and accidents
involving members of the service in the performance of their duties shall be
reported immediately by the Captain, to the Mayor and Town Council.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-10: RECORDS AND REPORT OF ACTIVITIES:
The Captain of the ambulance service shall keep or cause to be kept, a complete
record of the activities of the service in accordance with the requirements of
the Wyoming State Emergency Medical Service Office. The Captain shall meet with
the Town Council upon request of the Council.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-11: FUNDING AND EXPENDITURES:
Monies shall be appropriated from the Ambulance Service Fund of the Town for
operating expenses of the ambulance service. In addition, the ambulance service
is authorized to raise funds and solicit donations through social activities,
for the purpose of defraying expenses of the service, which funds shall be
turned over to and earmarked by the Treasurer for disbursement in accordance
with applicable ordinances and Wyoming Statutes for emergency medical service
purposes. No member of the department or any other person shall contract any
indebtedness on behalf of the service unless authorized to do so with approval
by the Mayor. If allowed by Wyoming Statutes, the service may maintain separate
accounts for funds received from public entities and funds received from
private sources.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-12: PROHIBITED ACTS AND ACTIVITIES:
   A.   Interfering With Ambulance Service:
      1.   No person shall enter or be allowed to enter the ambulance garage
unless accompanied by a member of the department, unless authorized so to enter
by a member of the department. No person nor member of the department shall use
any of the emergency service apparatus at emergencies or otherwise unless
acting under orders of the officer of the service in charge of the emergency,
nor shall any person interfere in any way with the service or any member of the
service in the performance of its, or his or her, duty.
      2.   Upon hearing the emergency alarm, all drivers of vehicles shall take
due warning and upon the approach of emergency vehicles shall move promptly to
the right curb and stop in order to leave the middle of the street clear for
passage of the emergency medical service apparatus. Vehicles shall not follow
emergency medical service apparatus nearer than one full block and shall not
proceed to any point within one full block of the emergency. This subsection
shall not apply to those vehicles driven by members of the service proceeding
to the emergency for the purpose of assistance. No vehicle shall be parked
within twenty feet (20') or before the entrance to any theater, hall, or other
building in which large assemblages are held.
   B.   Lending Emergency Apparatus: Emergency apparatus and other Town
property in the charge of the service shall not be loaned or rented except by
permission of the Captain of the service and the Mayor; provided, that such
equipment may be used for Municipal purposes if a service member is present.
   C.   False Emergency Alarm: No person shall knowingly give a false emergency
alarm except those for test purposes given or caused to be given by the Captain
of the service. No person shall interfere with any part of the emergency alarm
system unless authorized to do so by the Captain.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-13: MEDICAL HAZARD; ABATEMENT:
In those instances in which a medical hazard or dangerous condition is found to
exist as provided in this chapter and the owner or proprietor of the premises
is not to be found within the Town, nor otherwise available upon the exertion
of reasonable effort upon the part of the Emergency Medical Service Captain, or
refuses or fails to remedy the hazard or condition, the Emergency Medical
Service Captain shall notify the Town Council at the next regular meeting of
the existence of the medical hazard or dangerous condition and the location
thereof and the fact that the proprietor is not available or that the
proprietor refuses or has failed to remedy the hazard or condition. If the
hazard is urgent, notification to the Town Council should be immediate. Upon
receipt of such notice, the Council is authorized to order the abatement of the
condition reported as provided in this chapter. The abatement shall be carried
out by the proper officer or officers of the Town, members of the ambulance
service or otherwise, and the expense of the abatement shall be paid out of the
Ambulance Service Fund of the Town Treasury and shall be included, together
with a surcharge equal to two hundred percent (200%) of such costs to cover
indirect administrative costs, in a bill charged against the owner of the
property within or upon which the medical hazard or dangerous condition was
found to exist.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-14: MEDICAL SERVICE PROTECTION BY OTHERS:
No groups or persons may provide emergency medical service protection and or
treatment on an organized basis unless and until such group has been organized
as directed by this chapter and its operations and procedures specifically
approved by the Town Council.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
5-3-15: PENALTY:
The penalty for violation of any provision of this chapter shall be as
specified in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day of an offense is constituted as a separate
offense.
(Ord. 204, 10-13-1997)
CHAPTER 4: FIRE ZONES
Section
5-4-1: Establishment Of Fire Zone
5-4-2: Prohibition Of Certain Building Practices Within Fire Zone
5-4-3: Penalty
5-4-1: ESTABLISHMENT OF FIRE ZONE:
For the purpose of protecting public health and safety, the Town fully adopts
the International Building Code and abolishes the one hundred twenty foot
(120') setback. The International Building Code is dedicated to the development
of better building construction and greater safety to the public uniformity in
building laws. The Code is founded on broad based principles that make possible
the use of new materials and new construction systems.
(Ord. 199, 5-19-1997)
5-4-2: PROHIBITION OF CERTAIN BUILDING PRACTICES WITHIN FIRE ZONE:
No commercial building, or addition to any commercial building, framed with
wood, shall hereafter be placed, built or erected within the Fire Zone as
designated in this chapter. The provisions of this section shall not prohibit
the installation, maintenance, repair or replacement of wood siding upon any
building within said Fire Zone, but shall prevent construction, alteration, or
reconstruction of any commercial building within said zone when such building
is framed with wood.
(1982 Code § 15.01.020)
5-4-3: PENALTY:
Any violation of this chapter shall be punished upon conviction as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 15.01.030)
CHAPTER 5: EXPLOSIVES AND FIREWORKS
Section
5-5-1: Licensing
5-5-2: Stands
5-5-3: Regulations And Requirements
5-5-4: Penalty
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 35-10-201 et seq.
5-5-1: LICENSING:
   A.   License Required; Fee: It shall be unlawful for any person to offer for
sale, sell or give away any fireworks within the Town without first obtaining a
license therefor and paying a yearly license fee of five hundred dollars
($500.00).
   B.   Application; Information: Any person applying for a license to offer
for sale, sell or give away any fireworks shall file with the Town Clerk a
sworn application in writing which shall contain the following information:
      1.   The name of applicant.
      2.   The permanent home address and local address of the applicant and
the representative thereof filing the application.
      3.   A description of the nature of the business to be conducted.
      4.   The place where the sale of the fireworks will take place, which
place must be approved by the Town Fire Chief prior to the issuance of the
license.
      5.   The applicant must apply each year and pay the license fee each
year.
(Ord. 209, 5-10-1999)
5-5-2: STANDS:
   A.   Permanent Stands: Permanent stands are buildings or structures which
have a foundation, are not moved or dismantled, have no wheels, and remain on
location year round.
      1.   Electrical service and structure wiring shall meet the current
adopted edition of the National Electrical Code.
      2.   Extension cords shall not be used for permanent wiring.
      3.   Florescent bulb covers are required on all fixtures.
      4.   A minimum of two (2) exits with exit signs posted over the doors and
the doors shall be a minimum of three feet (3') wide and six feet (6') to eight
feet (8') high.
      5.   Fire extinguishers, 2A:20B.C., with current inspection tags, mounted
not over sixty inches (60") above the floor at each exit.
      6.   No smoking signs posted inside the structure.
      7.   No smoking within fifty feet (50') signs posted outside of the
structure on all four (4) sides.
      8.   All trash shall be picked up around the structure and weeds shall be
kept two inches (2") within seventy five feet (75') of the structure.
      9.   The applicant must submit a copy of their insurance with a one
million dollar ($1,000,000.00) limit and the Town listed as additional insured.
   B.   Temporary Stands: Temporary stands are buildings and structures with no
foundations, and can be moved from one location to another.
      1.   Must obtain a building permit each year.
      2.   Must have written permission from landowner.
      3.   Must submit a copy of their insurance.
      4.   Must meet the Town’s existing setback regulations.
      5.   The temporary buildings, etc., may only be in the same location for
a maximum of 90 days.
      6.   The structure must be nice in appearance, painted, skirted, etc.
      7.   There shall be two (2) exits, one on each end of the stand.
      8.   Fire extinguishers, 2A:20B.C., with current inspection tags, mounted
not over sixty inches (60") above the floor at each exit.
      9.   No smoking signs posted inside the stand.
      10.   No smoking within 50 feet of signs posted outside the stand on all
four (4) sides.
      11.   All trash picked up around the stand and weeds shall be cut less
than two inches (2") within seventy five feet (75') of the stand.
      12.   Applicant will not be issued a business license until the above
requirements are met.
5-5-3: REGULATIONS AND REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Minimum Age: No license or selling of fireworks shall be issued to any
person who has not attained the age of nineteen (19) years and no person will
sell fireworks unless they are nineteen (19) years of age and older.
   B.   Storage Areas: It shall be unlawful to possess, store or use any
fireworks within one hundred feet (100') of any gasoline bulk station or
storage area, or any building or fuel source in which gasoline or volatile
liquids or gases are dispensed.
   C.   Dry Conditions: The Council shall have the right to determine whether
or not conditions are too dry for either selling or shooting fireworks. If the
Council determines conditions are too dry, they can cause both selling and
shooting of fireworks to be illegal in the Town until such time as they feel it
is safe.
(Ord. 209, 5-10-1999)
5-5-4: PENALTY:
Violation of this chapter constitutes a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall
be punishable as specified in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
CHAPTER 6: ANIMAL CONTROL
Section
5-6-1: Definitions
5-6-2: Permit Requirements
5-6-3: Number Of Dogs Or Cats Permitted
5-6-4: Restraint Required; At Large Prohibited
5-6-5: Noisy Dogs
5-6-6: Harboring Vicious Dogs
5-6-7: Interfering With Live Dog Traps
5-6-8: Impounding
5-6-9: Penalty
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-1-103(a)(xiv)
5-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, each of the following terms are defined as follows:
AT LARGE: Every dog shall be considered running at large when it is physically
off the real property of the owner of the dog, and not under immediate
restraint of a competent person.
NOISY DOG: Any dog which habitually, constantly or frequently disturbs the
sleep, peace or quiet of any neighborhood or person.
OWNER: Any person, group of persons, association of persons or corporation who
shall own, keep or harbor any dog, or permit the same to habitually remain or
be fed in or about such owners’ premises.
RESTRAINT: A dog is under restraint only when controlled by a leash or when in
the immediate company of a competent person and obedient to that person’s
command, or in a vehicle on a street or other place not within the property
limits of the owner.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-2: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Required; Exceptions; Nonresidents:
      1.   No person shall, without first obtaining a permit therefor, in
writing from the Town Clerk or administrative official, own, keep, harbor or
have custody of, any dog over three (3) months of age. A permit, if not
revoked, shall be valid from the date of issuance, until June 30 of the year
following the year of issue. Every owner shall obtain a new permit each year.
The provisions of this subsection shall not apply to dogs brought into Town for
the purpose of participating in any dog show, nor to seeing eye dogs assisting
blind persons, when such dogs are properly trained to assist blind persons, for
the purpose of aiding them in going from place to place. Any other dog which is
the property of a nonresident of the Town, must have a valid license or permit
issued by another municipal corporation.
      2.   Dogs which are the property of nonresident owners, and which have
not been properly licensed by another municipality corporation, may be taken up
and impounded in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
   B.   Application For Permit: The owner shall state at the time application
is made for a permit and upon printed form provided for such purpose, his name
and address, and the name, breed, color and sex of each dog owned or kept by
him, whether such dog has been spayed or neutered, and in the case of spayed or
neutered dogs the owner shall submit a certificate from a licensed veterinarian
that his dog or dogs have been spayed or neutered. At the time of application
for permit, the owner shall also present a certificate of rabies vaccination in
accordance with this chapter.
   C.   Conditions Of Issuance: Permits issued in accordance with this chapter
are conditioned upon the requirement for humane care of the owner’s dog and for
compliance by the owner with all provisions of this chapter and other
applicable State and local laws. The Town Clerk or administrative official may
revoke any permit if the person holding the permit refuses or fails to comply
with this chapter or any State or local law governing cruelty to animals or the
keeping of animals. Any person whose permit is revoked shall, within ten (10)
days thereafter, shall remove the dogs from the town limits by such person and
no part of the permit fee shall be refunded. If any person whose permit is
revoked shall fail to humanely dispose of all dogs being owned, kept or
harbored by such person as required in this chapter, such dogs may be impounded
by the administrative official and thereafter humanely disposed of.
   D.   Issuance Of Permit; Fee; Tags:
      1.   Upon showing by any applicant for a permit, that he or she is
prepared to comply with the conditions of issuance, a permit shall be issued,
upon the payment of ten dollars ($10.00).
      2.   Upon issuing a permit to keep any dog, the Town Clerk or
administrative official, shall issue to the owner, a metallic or durable
plastic tag, stamped with an identifying number, and with the year of issuance,
and so designed that it may conveniently be fastened to the dog’s collar or
harness by the owner, and shall be worn at all times when the dog is off the
premises of its owner. The Town Clerk shall maintain a record of the
identifying numbers and shall make the record available to the public.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-3: NUMBER OF DOGS OR CATS PERMITTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep or harbor at any single-family
residence in the Town more than six (6) dogs or cats more than four (4) months
of age, excepting duly licensed kennel operators.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-4: RESTRAINT REQUIRED; AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
All dogs shall be kept under restraint. No dog shall be allowed to run at large
within the Town limits. It shall be presumed of the owner of any dog impounded
pursuant hereto, which dog has previously been impounded pursuant hereto, that
such owner has knowingly allowed such dog to run at large.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-5: NOISY DOGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep or harbor within the limits of
the Town any dog which by its barking, howling or yelping, habitually disturbs
the quiet of any neighborhood or person.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-6: HARBORING VICIOUS DOGS:
No person shall have, keep or harbor, or allow to be kept or harbored, upon any
premises occupied by him, or in or under his charge or control, any notoriously
vicious or cross dog, or any dog that may manifest a disposition to bite
anyone, without having the same adequately secured and muzzled. Upon the
conviction of any person under the provisions of this section, if it shall
appear to the Municipal Judge that said dog is still living, said Judge may in
addition to the punishment provided for violation of this chapter order the
Chief of Police or any police officer, to forthwith cause such dog to be
humanely destroyed, and for that purpose any such police officer charged with
such duty shall have the right to enter upon any premises within the Town.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-7: INTERFERING WITH LIVE DOG TRAPS:
No person shall interfere, tamper with or in any way affect the operation of
any live dog trap maintained or utilized by the administrative official or any
police officer of the Town.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-8: IMPOUNDING:
   A.   Dogs At Large: Any police officer or the administrative official of the
Town shall take up and impound every dog found or known to be running at large
and shall do so without making or requiring a complaint therefor and shall
place such dog in the local animal shelter. A citation may be issued to the dog
owner as specified in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
   B.   Notice Of Impounding:
      1.   Upon the impounding of any dog in accordance with the provisions of
this chapter, the administrative official, or the Police Department, shall
exert reasonable efforts to ascertain the ownership of such dog. If by a permit
tag or other means the owner can be identified, the administrative official or
Police Department shall notify the owner by telephone, in person or by writing
if the dog has been impounded. Such notice shall contain a general description
of the dog and date of impounding.
      2.   If the owner of the impounded dog is not ascertained as stated
above, a notice of the impounding of such dog shall be posted at the Town Hall,
which notice shall contain a general description of the impounded dog and the
date of impounding.
   C.   Reclaiming Impounded Dogs:
      1.   Only the owner may reclaim or redeem an impounded dog. The owner is
responsible for any and all fees and other requirements required by the local
animal shelter.
      2.   Any and all rules and regulations of the local animal shelter shall
be applicable under this chapter.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
5-6-9: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction of the violation hereof, shall be punishable
as specified by section
 1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord., 8-9-2000)
CHAPTER 7: OFFENSES
Section
5-7-1: Interference With Police Department
5-7-2: Following Fire Apparatus And/Or Driving Over Fire Hose
5-7-3: Assault
5-7-4: Assault And Battery
5-7-5: Affray
5-7-6: Petit Larceny
5-7-7: Receiving Stolen Goods
5-7-8: Shoplifting
5-7-9: Public Indecency
5-7-10: Cruelty To Animals
5-7-11: Public Intoxication
5-7-12: Breach Of Peace
5-7-13: Discharging Firearms
5-7-14: Disorderly Conduct
5-7-15: False Fire Alarms
5-7-16: False Call For Police
5-7-17: Interfering With Fire Alarm System
5-7-18: Gambling
5-7-19: Malicious Mischief
5-7-20: Possession Of Drug Paraphernalia
5-7-21: Criminal Trespass
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS title 6
5-7-1: INTERFERENCE WITH POLICE DEPARTMENT:
No person shall resist any police officer, any member of the Police Department,
or any person duly empowered with police authority while in the discharge or
apparent discharge of his duty, or in any way interfere with or hinder such
officer in the discharge of his duty and, upon conviction thereof, such person
shall be punished as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.010)
5-7-2: FOLLOWING FIRE APPARATUS AND/OR DRIVING OVER FIRE HOSE:
   A.   Following Fire Apparatus: The driver of any vehicle other than one on
any official business shall not follow any fire apparatus traveling in response
to a fire alarm, closer than five hundred feet (500'), or drive into or park
such vehicle within the block where any fire apparatus has stopped in answer to
a fire alarm. Any violation of this section shall be punished as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code.
   B.   Driving Over Fire Hose: No vehicle shall be driven over any unprotected
hose of the Fire Department when laid down on any street or private driveway to
be used at any fire or alarm of fire, without the consent of the Fire
Department official in command. Any violation of this subsection shall be
punished as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 3.01.020)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-23, 31-5-232
5-7-3: ASSAULT:
Whoever, having the present ability to do so, unlawfully attempts to commit a
violent injury on the person of another, is guilty of assault and shall be
punished, upon conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.030)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-2-501
5-7-4: ASSAULT AND BATTERY:
Whoever, in a rude, insolent or angry manner, unlawfully touches another, is
guilty of assault and battery, and shall be punished, upon conviction, as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.040)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-2-501
5-7-5: AFFRAY:
If two (2) or more persons by agreement fight in any public place, the persons
so offending are guilty of an affray and shall be punished, upon conviction, as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.050)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-6-101
5-7-6: PETIT LARCENY:
Whoever unlawfully steals, takes and carries, leads or drives away the personal
goods of another, of the value of any sum less than one hundred dollars
($100.00), is guilty of petit larceny and, upon conviction, shall be punished
as provided in section
 1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.060)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-3-402
5-7-7: RECEIVING STOLEN GOODS:
Whoever buys, receives, conceals or aids in the concealment of anything of
value, which has been stolen, embezzled or taken by false pretense, knowing the
same to have been stolen, embezzled or obtained by false pretense, shall be
punished, upon conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.070)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-3-402, 6-3-403
5-7-8: SHOPLIFTING:
   A.   Prohibition: Any person who wilfully conceals or wilfully takes
possession of any goods offered for sale by a wholesale or retail store or
other mercantile establishment, without the knowledge or consent of the owner
thereof and with intent to convert the goods to his own use without paying the
purchase price therefor is guilty of shoplifting.
   B.   Detain, Interrogate: Any peace officer, merchant or merchant’s employee
who has reasonable cause to believe that a person has committed the crime of
shoplifting, as defined in subsection A of this section, may detain and
interrogate such person in regard thereto in a reasonable manner and for a
reasonable time.
   C.   Penalty: Any person violating the provisions of this section shall,
upon conviction, be punished in accordance with the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.080)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-3-405
5-7-9: PUBLIC INDECENCY:
Whoever, being over fourteen (14) years of age, makes an indecent exposure of
his or her person in a public place, where there are other persons to be
offended or annoyed thereby, is guilty of public indecency and shall, upon
conviction, be punished as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.090)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-4-201
5-7-10: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
Whoever inhumanly, unnecessarily or cruelly beats, injures or otherwise abuses
any dumb animal within the limits of the Town is guilty of cruelty to animals
and shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.100)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-3-203
5-7-11: PUBLIC INTOXICATION:
If any person is drunk, or is in a state of intoxication on any highway, street
or thoroughfare or other public place within the Town, such person is guilty of
a misdemeanor and shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided as provided
in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.110)
5-7-12: BREACH OF PEACE:
Whoever, by any loud or unnecessary talking or by any threatening, abusive,
profane or obscene language, or violent actions, or by any other rude behavior
interrupts or disturbs the peace of any inhabitant of the Town is guilty of a
breach of peace and shall be punished, upon conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.120)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-6-102
5-7-13: DISCHARGING FIREARMS:
No person shall fire or discharge any gun, pistol, revolver or firearm of any
description within the Town limits.
(1982 Code § 13.01.130)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-8
5-7-14: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
   A.   Prohibitions: A person shall be deemed guilty of disorderly conduct if
he wilfully:
      1.   Commits an act in a violent manner toward another whereby the
property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged;
      2.   Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct
so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another;
      3.   Obstructs, either single or together with other persons, the flow of
vehicular or pedestrian traffic on any public way in the Town and refuses to
clear such obstruction when ordered to do so by the police or other lawful
authority;
      4.   Fails to obey a lawful order to disperse by a police officer, when
known to be such an official, where one or more persons are committing acts of
disorderly conduct in the immediate vicinity, and the public health and safety
is immediately threatened;
      5.   Resists or obstructs the performance of duties by police or any
other authorized official of the Municipality, when known to be such an
official;
      6.   Commits an act in a violent and tumultuous manner toward another
whereby that other is placed in danger of his life, limb or health;
      7.   Uses abusive, profane or obscene language in any public place.
   B.   Penalty: Any person convicted of disorderly conduct shall be punished
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.140)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-6-102, 15-1-103(a)(xvi)(C)
5-7-15: FALSE FIRE ALARMS:
No person shall knowingly give a false alarm of any fire, except those for test
purposes given or caused to be given by the Fire Department. Any violation of
this section shall be punished, upon conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.150)
5-7-16: FALSE CALL FOR POLICE:
No person shall knowingly call any police officer to any place by falsely
giving such officer to understand that he is needed or wanted in any place as
such officer. Any violation of this section shall be punished, upon conviction,
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.160)
5-7-17: INTERFERING WITH FIRE ALARM SYSTEM:
No person shall interfere with any part of the fire alarm system of the Town
unless so authorized by the Fire Department. Any violation of this section
shall be punished, upon conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.170)
5-7-18: GAMBLING:
   A.   Prohibition: No person shall play, deal carry on or conduct any game
whatsoever or any plan, scheme or device for money or anything of value by
means of cards, dice, slot machines, lotteries, or any contrivance, means,
device or machine within the Municipality.
(1982 Code § 13.01.180)
   B.   Allowing Gambling On Premises: No person shall knowingly permit
subsection A of this section to be violated in or upon the premises owned,
managed or controlled by him.
(1982 Code § 13.01.190)
   C.   Confiscation Of Devices: It shall be the duty of the Chief of Police to
seize any game, device, cards, tools or implements or other articles or things
designed for the purpose of gambling, employed or used by or in the possession
of parties arrested for gambling, and the same shall be disposed of in
accordance with the order of a court of competent jurisdiction.
(1982 Code § 13.01.200)
   D.   Penalty: Any violation of this section shall be punished, upon
conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-7-101 et seq.
5-7-19: MALICIOUS MISCHIEF:
No person shall wantonly or mischievously break or destroy, in manner, any
property of another. Any violation of this section shall be punished, upon
conviction, as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 13.01.210)
5-7-20: POSSESSION OF DRUG PARAPHERNALIA:
The term “drug paraphernalia” means all equipment, products and materials of
any kind which are used intended for use, or designed for use, in planting,
propagating, cultivating, growing, harvesting, manufacturing compounding,
converting, producing, processing, preparing, testing, analyzing, packaging,
repackaging, storing, containing, concealing, injecting, ingesting, inhaling or
otherwise introducing into the human body a controlled substance, as defined by
the Wyoming Controlled Substances Act, Wyoming Statutes section 35-7-1001, of
the Act. Said Act by this reference is hereby incorporated herein as if fully
set forth. It includes, but is not limited to:
   A.   Kits used, intended for use, or designed for use in planting,
propagating, cultivating, growing or harvesting of any species of plant which
is a controlled substance or from which a controlled substance can be derived;
   B.   Kits used, intended for use, or designed for use in manufacturing,
compounding, converting, producing, processing, or preparing controlled
substances;
   C.   Isomerization devices used, intended for use, or designed for use in
increasing the potency of any species of plant which is a controlled substance;
   D.   Testing equipment used, intended for use, or designed for use in
identifying, or in analyzing the strength, effectiveness or purity of
controlled substances;
   E.   Scales and balances used, intended for use, or designed for use in
weighing or measuring controlled substances;
   F.   Diluents and adulterants, such as quinine hydrochloride, mannitol,
mannite, dextrose and lactose, used, intended for use, or designed for use in
cutting controlled substances.
   G.   Separation gins and sifters used, intended for use or designed for use
in removing twigs and seeds from, or in otherwise cleaning or refining,
marijuana;
   H.   Blenders, bowls, containers, spoons and mixing devices used, intended
for use, or designed for use in compounding controlled substances;
   I.   Capsules, balloons, envelopes and other containers used, intended for
use, or designed for use in packaging small quantities of controlled
substances;
   J.   Containers and other objects used, intended for use, or designed for
use in storing or concealing controlled substances;
   K.   Hypodermic syringes, needles and other objects used, intended for use,
or designed for use in parentally injecting controlled substances into the
human body;
   L.   Objects used, intended for use, or designed for use in ingesting,
inhaling, or otherwise introducing marijuana, cocaine, hashish, or hashish oil
into the human body:
      1.   Metal, wooden, acrylic, glass, stone, plastic or ceramic pipes, with
or without screens, permanent screens, hashish heads or punctured metal bowls;
      2.   Water pipes;
      3.   Carburetion masks;
      4.   Smoking and carburetion masks;
      5.   Roach clips, meaning objects used to hold burning material, such as
marijuana.
(Ord. 289, 6-5-2013)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 35-7-1001
5-7-21: CRIMINAL TRESPASS:
   A.   Prohibition: A person is guilty of criminal trespass if he enters or
remains on or in the land or premises of another person, knowing he is not
authorized to do so, or after being notified to depart or to not trespass. For
purposes of this section, notice is given by:
      1.   Personal communication to the person by the owner or occupant, or
his agent, or by a peace officer; or
      2.   Posting of signs reasonably likely to come to attention of
intruders;
      3.   Posting of signs reasonably likely to come to the attention of
intruders.
   B.   Penalty: Criminal trespass is a misdemeanor, punishable as provided for
in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 291, 6-5-2013)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 6-3-303
TITLE 6: MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
TRAFFIC CODE   1
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT   1A
LICENSES, REGISTRATION, INSURANCE   2
OPERATION OF VEHICLES   3
CHAPTER 1: TRAFFIC CODE
Section
6-1-1: Traffic Code Sections Adopted
6-1-2: References In Traffic Code
6-1-3: Penalty
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-108 (local authority)
6-1-1: TRAFFIC CODE SECTIONS ADOPTED:
Wyoming Statutes sections 31-5-101 through 31-5-110, 31-5-112 through 31-5-119,
31-5-121 through 31-5-233, 31-5-301 through 31-5-407, 31-5-503 through 31-5-706
and 31-5-901 through 31-5-960, the same being portions of the Uniform Act
Regulating Traffic on Highways, are adopted by reference and incorporated
herein as part of this title as fully as if completely set forth herein. One
copy of such Uniform Act shall be kept on file in the Office of Town Clerk for
examination and inspection.
(1982 Code § 4.01.010)
Statutory reference:
   Pursuant to WS § 15-1-119
6-1-2: REFERENCES IN TRAFFIC CODE:
   A.   Justice Of The Peace: Whenever reference is made in the Uniform Act
Regulating Traffic on Highways to “Justice of the Peace”, said words are
amended to and intended to refer to the Judge of the Town or Municipal Court of
Thayne, Wyoming, as appropriate.
(1982 Code § 4.01.020)
   B.   Streets: Whenever reference is made in the Uniform Act Regulating
Traffic on Highways, to the word “highways” or “State highway”, the same means
and includes streets within the Town of Thayne, State of Wyoming.
(1982 Code § 4.01.030)
   C.   Governing Body: Whenever reference is made in the Uniform Act
Regulating Traffic on Highways to “governing body” or “local authorities”, the
same means and includes the Town Council of the Town of Thayne, Wyoming.
(1982 Code § 4.01.040)
6-1-3: PENALTY:
   A.   Violation: It is a misdemeanor for any person to violate any of the
provisions of this title, unless such violation is declared to be a felony by
State law.
   B.   Penalty: Every person convicted of a misdemeanor for a violation of any
of the provisions of this chapter for which another penalty is not provided
shall be punished as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Evidence of a prior conviction or convictions shall not be
introduced during the trial of any case, but shall be introduced only after the
completion of the trial for the purpose of determining the penalty to be
imposed upon a conviction hereunder.
(1982 Code § 4.01.250)
ARTICLE A: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
Section
6-1A-1: Arrest Procedures; Appearance; Citations
6-1A-2: Traffic Citations
6-1A-1: ARREST PROCEDURES; APPEARANCE; CITATIONS:
   A.   Authority; Offenses: Whenever a person is arrested for any violation of
this title, the authority of a police officer to make an arrest is the same as
upon an arrest for a felony when the officer has reasonable and probable
grounds to believe that the person arrested has committed any of the following
offenses:
      1.   Negligent homicide or homicide by vehicle;
      2.   Driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while under
the influence of intoxicating liquor or any controlled substance;
      3.   Failure to stop, failure to give information in the event of an
accident resulting in death or personal injuries as prescribed in Wyoming
Statutes sections 31-5-1101 and 31-5-1103;
      4.   Failure to stop or give information in the event of an accident
resulting in damage to a vehicle or to fixtures or other property legally upon
or adjacent to a highway as prescribed in Wyoming Statutes sections 31-5-1102,
31-5-1104 and 31-5-1105;
      5.   Reckless driving.
   B.   Whenever any person is arrested as authorized in this section, he shall
be taken without unnecessary delay before the proper court as specified in
subsection
 6-1A-2A8, except, that in the case of either of the offenses designated in
subsections A4 and A5 of this section, a police officer shall have the same
discretion as is provided in other cases in subsection D of this section.
   C.   Taken To Court: Whenever any person is halted by a police officer for
any violation of this title, he shall be taken without unnecessary delay before
the proper court as specified in subsection
6-1A- 2A8, in the following case: when the person demands an immediate
appearance before a judge.
   D.   Citation; Taken To Judge: Whenever any person is halted by a police
officer for any violation of this title and is not required to be taken before
a court as hereinbefore provided, the person shall, in the discretion of the
officer, either be given a traffic citation or be taken without unnecessary
delay before the proper judge, as specified in subsection
6-1A-2A8 of this article, in any of the following cases:
      1.   When the person does not furnish satisfactory evidence of identity
or when the officer has reasonable and probable grounds to believe the person
will disregard a written promise to appear in court;
      2.   When the person is charged with a violation of Wyoming Statutes
section 31-5-959, relating to vehicles transporting explosives.
   E.   Applicability To Residents, Nonresidents: All of the provisions of this
section apply both to residents and nonresidents of this State, except the
special provisions in this section which shall govern in respect to
nonresidents under the circumstances hereinafter stated:
      1.   A police officer at the scene of a traffic accident may arrest
without a warrant any driver of a vehicle who is a nonresident of this State
and who is involved in the accident when, based upon personal investigation,
the officer has reasonable and probable grounds to believe that the person has
committed any offense under the provisions of this title in connection with the
accident;
      2.   Whenever any person is arrested under the provisions of this
subsection, he shall be taken without unnecessary delay before the proper
court, as specified in subsection
6-1A-2A8 of this article.
(1982 Code § 4.01.260)
6-1A-2: TRAFFIC CITATIONS:
   A.   Requirements:
      1.   Whenever a person is halted by a police officer for any violation of
this title punishable as a misdemeanor, and is not taken before a judge, the
officer shall prepare a written traffic citation containing a notice to appear
in court.
      2.   The time specified in the notice to appear must be at least five (5)
days after the alleged violation unless the person charged with the violation
shall demand an earlier hearing.
      3.   The place specified in the notice to appear must be before a judge
as designated in subsection A8 of this section.
      4.   The person charged with the violation in which event the officer
shall deliver a copy of the citation to the person, and thereupon, the officer
shall not take the person into physical custody for the violation.
      5.   The police justice of the Town may designate specified offenses
under the motor vehicle and traffic ordinances of the Town in respect to which
payment of fines may be accepted by paying the amount designated without
appearance before the police justice, and shall specify by suitable schedules
the amount of such fines, provided such fines are within the limits declared by
ordinance.
      6.   Any officer violating any of the provisions of this section is
guilty of misconduct in office and shall be subject to removal from office.
      7.   Except for felonies and those offenses enumerated in subsections
 6-1A-1A1, A2 and A3 of this article, a police officer at the scene of a
traffic accident may issue a written traffic citation, as provided in
subsection A of this section, to any driver of a vehicle involved in the
accident when, based upon personal investigation, the officer has reasonable
and probable grounds to believe that the person has committed any offense under
the provisions of this title in connection with the accident.
      8.   Whenever any person is taken before a judge or is given a written
traffic citation containing a notice to appear before a judge as hereinbefore
provided, the judge shall be a judge within the Town in which the offense
charged is alleged to have been committed and who has jurisdiction of the
offense and is nearest or most accessible with reference to the place where the
alleged violation occurred.
      9.   Whenever any person is taken into custody by an officer for the
purpose of taking him before a judge or court as authorized or required in this
title upon any charge other than the offenses enumerated in subsections
6-1A-1A1, A2 and A3 of this article, and no judge is available at the time of
arrest, and there is no bail schedule established by any court and no lawfully
designated court clerk or other public officer who is available and authorized
to accept bail upon behalf of the court, the person shall be released from
custody upon the issuance to him of a written traffic citation.
(1982 Code § 4.01.280)
   B.   Appearance:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to violate his written promise
to appear given to an officer upon the issuance of a traffic citation
regardless of the disposition of the charge for which such citation was
originally issued.
      2.   A written promise to appear in court may be complied with by an
appearance by counsel.
(1982 Code § 4.01.290)
   C.   Forms:
      1.   Appropriate forms for traffic citations containing notices to appear
which shall be issued in books with citations in triplicate and meeting the
requirements of subsection A of this section.
      2.   The Chief of Police shall be responsible for the issuance of such
books and shall maintain a record of every such book and each citation
contained therein issued to individual police officers and shall require and
retain a receipt for every book so issued.
(1982 Code § 4.01.290)
   D.   Disposition; Records:
      1.   Every police officer, upon issuing a traffic citation to an alleged
violator of any provision of this title, shall deposit the original or a copy
of such traffic citation with the court having jurisdiction over the alleged
offense.
      2.   Upon the deposit of the original or a copy of such traffic citation
with the court, the original or copy of such traffic citation may be disposed
of only by trial in such court or other official action by a judge of such
court, including forfeiture of the bail, or by the deposit of sufficient bail
with or payment of a fine to the court by the person to whom such traffic
citation has been issued by the police officer.
      3.   It shall be unlawful and official misconduct for any police officer
or other officer or public employee to dispose of a traffic citation or copies
thereof or of the record of the issuance of the same in a manner other than as
required herein.
      4.   The Chief of Police shall require the return to him of a copy of
every traffic citation issued by an officer under his supervision to an alleged
violator and of all copies of every traffic citation which has been spoiled or
upon which any entry has been made and not issued to an alleged violator.
      5.   The Chief of Police shall also maintain or cause to be maintained in
connection with every traffic citation issued by an officer under his
supervision a record of the disposition of the charge by the court in which the
original or copy of the traffic citation was deposited.
(1982 Code § 4.01.300)
   E.   Illegal Cancellation; Audits; Annual Publication:
      1.   Any person who cancels or solicits the cancellation of any traffic
citation, in any manner other than as provided in subsection A of this section,
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
      2.   Every record of traffic citations issued under the authority of the
ordinances of the Municipality shall be audited annually by the appropriate
fiscal officer of the Municipality.
(1982 Code § 4.01.310)
   F.   When Deemed Lawful Compliant: In the event the form of citation
provided under subsection A of this section includes information and is sworn
to as required under the general laws of this State in respect to a complaint
charging commission of the offense alleged in such citation to have been
committed, then such citation when filed with a court having jurisdiction shall
be deemed to be a lawful complaint for the purpose of prosecution under this
title.
(1982 Code § 4.02.320)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-1205
CHAPTER 2: LICENSES, REGISTRATION, INSURANCE
Section
6-2-1: Driver’s License
6-2-2: Registration Of Vehicles
6-2-3: Liability Coverage
6-2-1: DRIVER’S LICENSE:
   A.   License Required: It is unlawful for any person to drive a motor
vehicle upon the streets of the Town unless such person has in his immediate
possession a valid operator’s license or chauffeur’s license issued by the
State of Wyoming or by his home state or county, as may be required by the laws
of the State of Wyoming, if such operator’s license or chauffeur’s license is
required of such person under the laws of his home state or country, and
displays the same upon demand of a police officer of this Town; provided,
however, that it shall be a defense to any charge under this subsection that
the person so charged produce in court an operator’s or chauffeur’s license as
above required theretofore issued to such person and valid at the time of his
arrest.
   B.   Restricted License: It is unlawful for any person to drive a motor
vehicle upon the streets of the Town in any manner in violation of the
restrictions imposed in a restricted operator’s license or chauffeur’s license
granted to him by the State of Wyoming or by his home state or country.
(1982 Code § 4.01.050)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-7-101
6-2-2: REGISTRATION OF VEHICLES:
Every vehicle at all times while being driven, stopped or parked upon the
streets or alleys of this Town shall be registered in the name of the owner
thereof and in accordance with the laws of the State and shall display in
proper position valid and unexpired registration plates or indicia of
registration, meeting the requirements of the laws of the State, clear and
distinct and free from defacement, mutilation, grease and other obscuring
matter, so as to be plainly visible and legible at all times; provided,
however, if such vehicle is not required to be registered in this State, the
indicia of registration issued by another state, territory, possession or
district of the United States or a foreign country, substantially complying
with the provisions hereof, shall be considered as compliance with this
section, in accordance with the laws of the State.
(1982 Code § 4.01.060)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-2-201 et seq.
6-2-3: LIABILITY COVERAGE:
   A.   Requirements: No owner of a motor vehicle currently required to be
registered or which is required to be registered within a period of time, shall
operate or permit the operation of his motor vehicle without having in full
force and effect a motor vehicle liability policy in amounts provided by
Wyoming Statutes section 31-9-405(b), or a bond in amounts provided by Wyoming
Statutes section 31-9-102(a)(xi).
   B.   Penalty: Violation of this subsection is a misdemeanor punishable by
imprisonment for not more than six (6) months, a fine of not less than two
hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00), or both. On a second or subsequent violation of this subsection, the
person may be fined not less than five hundred dollars ($500.00) nor more than
one thousand five hundred dollars ($1,500.00), imprisoned for not more than six
(6) months, or both. In addition to the fine or imprisonment imposed for a
second or subsequent violation of this section, the Judge shall require the
defendant to deliver the registration and license plates of the vehicle
involved to the county treasurer for the county where the citation was issued,
and the registration and license plates shall be held by the county treasurer
until such time as the Judge determines that the defendant has met all
obligations imposed by law.
(Ord. 285, 6-5-2013)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-4-103
CHAPTER 3: OPERATION OF VEHICLES
Section
6-3-1: Speed Limits Generally
6-3-2: Stop And Yield Intersections
6-3-3: Stopping Or Standing Prohibited In Specified Places
6-3-4: Emerging From Alleys, Driveways Or Buildings
6-3-5: Parking During Snowplowing
6-3-6: Parking Within Ten Feet Of Fire Station Entrance
6-3-7: Blocking Access
6-3-8: Towing Of Illegally Parked Vehicles
6-3-9: Snowmobiles
6-3-10: Prohibitions On Walking Paths
6-3-11: Use Of Handheld Wireless Communication Devices
6-3-12: Open Containers Of Alcoholic Beverages
6-3-13: Accident Reports Required
6-3-14: Careless Driving
6-3-1: SPEED LIMITS GENERALLY:
   A.   No person shall drive a vehicle on a street at a speed greater than is
reasonable and prudent under the conditions and having regard to the actual and
potential hazards then existing.
   B.   1.   Twenty (20) miles per hour when passing a school building, or the
grounds thereof, or a school crossing, during school recess or while children
are going to or leaving school during opening or closing hours; provided, that
the presence of such school building, ground thereof or school crossing is
indicated plainly by signs or signals conforming to the provisions hereof.
      2.   Twenty five (25) miles per hour in any town road, unless otherwise
posted.
(1982 Code § 4.01.070)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-109(a)(ix)
6-3-2: STOP AND YIELD INTERSECTIONS:
When local authorities have designated through streets, through highways and
have erected signs or yield signs at specified entrances thereto or have
designated an intersection as a stop intersection or as a yield intersection,
except when directed to proceed by a police officer or traffic control signal,
every driver of a vehicle approaching a stop intersection indicated by a stop
sign shall stop before entering the crosswalk, shall stop at a clearly marked
stop line, but if none, then at the point nearest the intersecting roadway
where the driver has a view of approaching traffic on the intersecting roadway
before entering the intersection; the driver of a vehicle approaching a yield
sign if required for safety to stop shall stop before entering the crosswalk on
the near side of the intersection, or in the event there is no crosswalk, at a
clearly marked stop line, but if none, then at the point nearest the
intersecting roadway where the driver has a view of approaching traffic on the
intersecting roadway.
(1982 Code § 4.01.090)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-503
6-3-3: STOPPING OR STANDING PROHIBITED IN SPECIFIED PLACES:
   A.   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to
avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law or the directions
of a police officer or traffic control device, in any of the following places:
      1.   On a sidewalk;
      2.   In front of a public or private driveway;
      3.   Within an intersection;
      4.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a street;
      5.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping;
      6.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
   B.   No person shall move a vehicle not lawfully under his control into any
such prohibited area or away from a curb such distance as is unlawful.
(1982 Code § 4.01.100)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-504
6-3-4: EMERGING FROM ALLEYS, DRIVEWAYS OR BUILDINGS:
The driver of a vehicle within a business or residence district emerging from
an alley, driveway or building shall stop such vehicle immediately prior to
driving onto a sidewalk or onto the sidewalk area extending across any alleyway
or driveway, and shall yield the right-of-way to any pedestrian as may be
necessary to avoid collision, and upon entering the roadway shall yield the
right-of-way to all vehicles approaching on such roadway.
(1982 Code § 4.01.110)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-506
6-3-5: PARKING DURING SNOWPLOWING:
No person shall park a vehicle on any street within the Town during the hours
of two thirty o’clock (2:30) A.M. and seven o’clock (7:00) A.M. at any time
from November 1 until March 31.
(1982 Code § 4.01.130)
6-3-6: PARKING WITHIN TEN FEET OF FIRE STATION ENTRANCE:
No person shall park a vehicle on any street within the Town within ten feet
(10') of the driveway entrance to any fire station.
(1982 Code § 4.01.140)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-109
6-3-7: BLOCKING ACCESS:
No person shall park a vehicle on any street within the Town which blocks
access from any driveway to a street within the Town.
(1982 Code § 4.01.150)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-504(a)(ii)(A)
6-3-8: TOWING OF ILLEGALLY PARKED VEHICLES:
Any vehicle found parked in violation of this title is hereby declared to be a
nuisance, and it may be summarily abated by removing such vehicle by or under
the directions or at the request of a police officer of the Town to a place of
storage within the Town or the towing company’s facility:
   A.   Notice: As soon as is reasonable under the circumstances, a written
notice that the vehicle has been impounded shall be mailed to the owner and
recorded lienholder, if there is one, of the vehicle at their last known
address as shown by the records of the Motor Vehicle Division of the Wyoming
Department of Revenue. If the license plates on the vehicle are from another
state, written notice shall be mailed to the Department of Motor Vehicles in
such state, requesting such department to notify that the same had been
impounded by the Police Department of the Town of Thayne and that the same will
be sold at public auction as is provided by the ordinances of the Town if not
claimed by the owner or his proper representatives, as provided by said Town
ordinance.
   B.   Criminal Proceedings: The impounding of a vehicle shall not prevent or
preclude the institution and prosecution of criminal proceedings against the
owner or operator of such impounded vehicles.
   C.   Requirements For Removal From Impound: Before the owner or his agent
shall be permitted to remove a vehicle which has been impounded he shall:
      1.   Furnish satisfactory evidence to the Police Department of his
identity and his ownership of the vehicle;
      2.   Request and obtain from the Police Department a written order
directed to the place of storage in which the vehicle is impounded, authorizing
the release of the vehicle to the owner or his agent upon the payment to the
place of storage of towing and storage charges reasonably incurred in the
towing and storage of the vehicle from the date of the impounding to the time
of presenting the order of release from the Police Department therefor;
      3.   Sign a written receipt of the vehicle and deliver the same to the
place of storage upon receiving the impounded vehicle.
   D.   Failure To Redeem; Notice; Sale: If at the expiration of thirty (30)
days after mailing notice provided for in subsection A of this section, such
vehicle is not redeemed by the owner or his proper representative, the Chief of
Police or his proper authorized agent shall proceed to sell the same at public
auction to the highest bidder after first giving at least ten (10) days’ notice
of the sale by publishing the notice at least once in a newspaper published in
Lincoln County, Wyoming, stating the time and place of such sale. Such notice
shall also describe the vehicle to be sold with reasonable certainty and shall
state whom, if anyone, the records of the Office of the Motor Vehicle Division
of the Department of Revenue show the same to belong, and, if there is one, the
name of the recorded lienholder. A copy of such notice as published shall be
mailed immediately after publication, to the owner or lienholder at their last
known address or their address shown on the records of the Motor Vehicle
Division of the Wyoming Department of Revenue. A copy of this notice as
published shall immediately, after publication, be mailed to the owner of the
place of storage. The money received by the Chief of Police or his authorized
agent, from the sale of any such vehicles shall be applied first to the actual
cost of towing and storage of such impounded vehicle, then to pay the actual
cost of advertising the notice of sale for each vehicle so impounded and the
balance, if any, shall then be paid to the Town Treasury to be used as
determined by the Town Council.
   E.   Application By Owner For Proceeds: At any time within one year from and
after such sale, the former owner of the vehicle sold, upon application to the
Town Council and upon presentation of satisfactory proof that he was the owner
of the vehicle sold, shall be paid the proceeds of such sale less the necessary
expense thereof and less the towing, impounding and storage charges and
administrative charges provided for in subsection D of this section.
   F.   Records Maintained: The Police Department shall keep a record of all
vehicles impounded by manufacturer’s trade name or make, body type, motor and
license number, and names and addresses of all persons claiming the same, and
such other descriptive matter as may identify such vehicles, the nature and
circumstances of the impounding thereof, and the violation on account of which
such vehicles were impounded, the date of such impounding thereof, and the name
and address of any person to whom any such vehicle is released.
(1982 Code § 4.01.060)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-504(a)(ii)(A)
6-3-9: SNOWMOBILES:
   A.   Defined: For purposes of this section, the following word shall have
the meaning ascribed to it by this section:
SNOWMOBILE: Any mechanically driven vehicle of a type which utilizes sled type
runners, or skis, or any endless tread or combination or these designated
primarily for operation over snow.
(1982 Code § 4.01.170)
   B.   Operational Requirements: It shall be unlawful for any person to drive
or operate any snowmobile at any place within the Municipality except in full
compliance with the following requirements:
      1.   Permitted Operations: Over snow vehicles shall operate only over
public roadways within the Town when the same shall be snow covered or snow
packed, unless such roadways are explicitly posted against snowmobile use, and
such vehicles shall not be operated on sidewalks or public property.
      2.   Operators License: No over snow vehicle shall be operated until the
driver thereof shall have in his possession a valid driver’s license issued
under the motor vehicles laws of the State.
      3.   Registration: No over snow vehicle shall be operated without a
proper and valid registration from the State, issued in accordance with Wyoming
Statutes sections 31-2-401 through 31-2-408.
      4.   Towing: No over snow vehicle shall pull any skier, sled or other
combination vehicle by rope, or flexible coupling; all sleighs or cutters shall
be safely and securely affixed to the over snow vehicle, by direct coupling,
solid tongue not to exceed twenty four inches (24") in length, or triangular
shaped tow bar not exceeding twenty four inches (24") in length, being securely
affixed to two (2) points on the sleigh or cutter, with one flexible joint at
the center of the over snow vehicle.
      5.   Safety Equipment: It shall be a misdemeanor for any person to drive
or move or for the owner to use or knowingly permit to be driven or moved on
any roadway or street any over snow vehicle or combination of vehicles which is
in such unsafe condition as to endanger any person or property which does not
contain those parts or if not at all times equipped with such equipment in
proper condition and adjustment as required by this section, or which is
equipped in any manner in violation hereof.
      6.   Mufflers: Every over snow vehicle shall be at all times equipped
with a muffler in good working order and in constant operation to prevent
excessive or unusual noise and annoying smoke.
      7.   Brakes: Every over snow vehicle shall be equipped with brakes
adequate to control the movement of and to stop and hold such vehicle.
      8.   Inspections: The City police and members of the State Highway Patrol
and County officials may at any time upon reasonable cause to believe that an
over snow vehicle is unsafe or not equipped as required by this section, or
that is not in proper adjustment or repair, may require the driver of such
vehicle to stop and submit such vehicle to an inspection and test with
reference thereto as may be appropriate. No person shall operate any vehicle
receiving notice with reference thereto as above provided except as may be
necessary to return such vehicle to the residence or place of business of the
owner or driver, or a garage, until said vehicle and its equipment have been
placed in proper repair and adjustment and otherwise made to conform to the
requirements of this section.
      9.   Rules Of The Road: Every operator or an over snow vehicle shall
observe all of the rules of the road pertaining to vehicles and in addition
shall yield the right-of-way to motor vehicles. All ordinances of the Town
pertaining to the operation of vehicles, to the extent that the same are not in
conflict herewith shall be applicable to the operation of over snow vehicles
and are adopted by reference and made a part hereof, the same as if set forth
fully herein.
      10.   Speed: No person shall operate, any over snow vehicle within the
incorporated limits of the Town at a speed in excess of the maximum speed
allowable for motor vehicles.
      11.   Method Of Travel: No person shall operate any over snow vehicle
within the incorporated limits of the Town where two (2) such vehicles are
abreast of each other, except while passing where permitted.
      12.   Penalties: Any person who shall violate one or more of the
provisions hereof, shall be subject to a penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(1982 Code § 4.01.180)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-2-401
6-3-10: PROHIBITIONS ON WALKING PATHS:
   A.   Prohibition: No person shall ride motorized vehicles, horses, four-
wheelers or snow machines on the Town walking paths.
   B.   Penalty: Violation of this section constitutes a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, is punishable as set forth in 1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 265, 11-10-2010)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-109
6-3-11: USE OF HANDHELD WIRELESS COMMUNICATION DEVICES:
No person shall operate a motor vehicle on a public street or highway while
using a handheld electronic wireless communication device to write, send or
read a text based communication.
(Ord. 286, 6-5-2013)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-237
6-3-12: OPEN CONTAINERS OF ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
   A.   Prohibition: No person shall consume, transport or possess any opened
alcoholic beverage in a motor vehicle which is in motion on a public street or
public highway, except as provided Wyoming Statutes section 31-5-235.
   B.   Penalty: Any person violating the provisions of this section shall:
      1.   For first conviction or a subsequent conviction not occurring within
one year after the first conviction, be punished by a fine of not more than two
hundred dollars ($200.00);
      2.   For a second conviction within one year after the first conviction,
be punished by a fine of not more than three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by
imprisonment for not more than thirty (30) days or both;
      3.   For a third or subsequent conviction within one year after the first
conviction, be punished by a fine of not more than five hundred dollars
($500.00) or by imprisonment for not more than six (6) months, or both.
(Ord. 287, 6-5-2013)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-235
6-3-13: ACCIDENT REPORTS REQUIRED:
Any person involved in an accident resulting in injuries to or death of any
person or damage to any vehicle is required to file with the Police Department
a report of such accident.
(1982 Code § 4.01.230)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-1105
6-3-14: CARELESS DRIVING:
Any person who drives any motor vehicle on any street or public property, or
upon any private property within this Municipality in a careless and imprudent
manner, without due regard for road and traffic conditions or the safety or
persons or property is guilty of careless driving. The offense of careless
driving shall be deemed to be a lessor included offense in the offense of
reckless driving.
(1982 Code § 4.01.240)
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 31-5-236
TITLE 7: PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL   1
RESTORATION STANDARDS FOR STREETS AND OTHER TOWN PROPERTY   2
TREE PROTECTION, ADMINISTRATION AND MANAGEMENT   3
RIGHT-OF-WAY PERMITS   4
