CHAPTER 1: SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL
Section
7-1-1: Definitions
7-1-2: Removal By Private Persons
7-1-3: Prohibited Deposits
7-1-4: Failure To Comply
7-1-5: Property In Road Right-Of-Way
 
7-1-6: Penalty
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-4-311
7-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases used in this chapter shall have the following
meanings unless a different meaning clearly appears from the context:
BUILDING INSPECTOR: The building inspector is the duly appointed Town building
inspector, Town administrative official and Town Engineer or, in his absence,
his duly designated and acting representative.
BUSINESS DAY: Any day not a Saturday, Sunday or a national holiday.
BUSINESS HOURS: The hours between eight o’clock (8:00) A.M. and five o’clock
(5:00) P.M. on any business day.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curb lines, or the lateral lines
of a roadway, and the adjacent property lines intended for the use of
pedestrians.
(1982 Code § 11.01.010)
7-1-2: REMOVAL BY PRIVATE PERSONS:
   A.   Required: Every person, partnership, corporation or other entity in
charge or control of any building or lot of land within the Town fronting or
abutting any sidewalk within the Municipal limits of the Town shall keep such
sidewalk free from snow, ice, encroachments or other obstructions which impede
the normal flow of pedestrians along such sidewalk. Snow and ice shall be
removed within twenty four (24) hours after the cessation of any fall of snow,
sleet or freezing rain, which creates an ice covered surface on a sidewalk.
   B.   Abrasives: In the event that snow and ice on a sidewalk have become so
hard that they cannot be removed without the likelihood of damage to a
sidewalk, the person or entity charged with the removal of such snow or ice,
within the time mentioned in subsection A of this section, shall cause enough
sand or other abrasive to be put on the sidewalk to make travel thereon
reasonably safe; and shall then, as soon thereafter as weather permits, cause
such sidewalk to be thoroughly cleaned.
(1982 Code § 11.01.020)
7-1-3: PROHIBITED DEPOSITS:
No person shall place snow or ice from private driveways on the maintained
portion of the Municipal streets, roads, parking lots, alleys or sidewalks.
(Ord. 266, 11-10-2010)
7-1-4: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
   A.   Work By Town: In the event of a failure of any person, partnership,
corporation or other entity to clear away or treat with abrasives and
subsequently clear away any snow and ice from any sidewalk as provided in this
chapter, or cause this to be done, the building inspector, as soon as practical
after such failure, may cause such work to be done by Town personnel or by
independent private persons or firms.
   B.   Record Maintained: The building inspector shall keep a record of the
exact cost of all work he causes to be done or contracts to be done in
accordance with this section.
   C.   Responsibility For Cost: Each person, partnership, corporation or
entity whose act or omission makes it necessary that the building inspector
causes work to be done or contracts work to be done in accordance with this
section shall be liable to the Town for the cost of such work plus an amount
equal to twenty percent (20%) of such cost for administration, record keeping
and notice. It shall be the duty of the Town Council to sue for these costs and
penalties, and it shall be the duty of the Town Attorney to assist in the
bringing of these suits.
(1982 Code § 11.01.040)
7-1-5: PROPERTY IN ROAD RIGHT-OF-WAY:
A.   Property owners shall not place trash containers or any property in the
road right-of-way. The town will not be responsible for damage to improvements,
landscaping, vehicles, or property that is in the road right-of-way and is
damaged by town operations (snow removal, grading, etc.). Any landscaping,
vehicles or property in the road right-of-way are placed there at the property
owner’s risk. The town has the right to remove any obstruction (e.g.
landscaping, driveways, etc.) placed by the property owner in the town’s right-
of-way at the property owner’s expense. Any damage to town equipment or to
other property because of these obstructions placed in the town’s right-of-way,
shall be charged to the property owner.
B.   Roads and persons placing property in the road right-of-way may be cited
and/or the property impounded at the owner’s expense.
C.   Parking is prohibited on any town street, town right-of-way, or town
parking lot from two o’clock (2:00) A.M. to six o’clock (6:00) A.M. from
November 1 to March 31.
(Ord. 395, - -2024)
7-1-6: PENALTY:
Any person, partnership, corporation or legal entity who violates any provision
of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punished in accordance with section 1-4-1 of this Code. Each day such
violation is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate
offense and shall be punishable as such under this chapter.
(1982 Code § 11.01.050; amd. Ord. 395, - -2024)
CHAPTER 2: RESTORATION STANDARDS
   FOR STREETS AND OTHER TOWN PROPERTY
Section
7-2-1: Adoption Of Standards
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-1-103(a)(xi)
7-2-1: ADOPTION OF STANDARDS:
The following standards are hereby adopted for the repair and/or restoration of
streets, roadways, driveways and other property within the Town, which has been
damaged by the installation of utilities or other authorized activities:
   A.   Trenching: The following standards shall apply to trenching or other
excavation under asphalt pavement:
      1.   Prior to any construction activities, asphalt shall be saw cut at
least one foot (1') wider than the proposed trench or other excavation. The one
foot (1') cut shall be made on each side, to form a “T-Cap” on the top of the
excavation. All pipelines shall be “bedded” and “shaded” with 1" minus granular
material in accordance with Wyoming DEQ standards. After the completion of the
construction activities, backfill shall be placed in eight inch (8") lifts.
Compaction shall be at least ninety five percent (95%) of the laboratory
density as determined by AASHTO Method T-91. Material shall be properly
moistened or dried to the optimum moisture content to ensure proper compaction.
The backfill material may be native, but no rock larger that six inches (6") in
diameter shall be allowed back into the trench.
      2.   The top eight inch (8") lift shall be imported aggregate base course
material meeting WDOT standard graduation “W”. It shall be compacted to ninety
five percent (95%) of its maximum density.
      3.   If a crossing of a Town street or roadway is required in order to
connect to a utility or for any other reason, boring underneath the street or
roadway shall be required. The only exception will be if boring is not feasible
as determined by the governing body of the Town.
      4.   Prior to replacement of asphalt, a six inch (6") thickness of
concrete shall be placed above the disturbed area. Asphalt shall then be
replaced at a compacted two inch (2") thickness or the equivalent thickness of
the existing asphalt, whichever is greater. Asphalt design mixture shall
conform with the most current WYDOT standard for flexible pavement (1/2-inch
minus aggregate size).
      5.   As an alternative to a “T-Cap”, the trench may be backfilled above
the pipe bedding material with “flowable backfill” up to the bottom elevation
of the pavement. Flowable backfill shall be fifty (50) to one hundred fifty
(150) psi max meeting the most current WYDOT mix design.
   B.   Conformance Exception: The trenches or other excavations under gravel
streets, roadways or driveways shall conform to the provisions of subsection A
of this section, except for the provisions pertaining to asphalt replacement.
   C.   Outside Of Roadways: Trenches or other excavation outside of roadways
shall conform to the following standards:
      1.   After completion of construction activities, backfill shall be
placed in eighteen inch (18") lifts and compacted to a minimum of eighty five
percent (85%) of the laboratory density determined by AASTO Method T-91.
Material shall be properly moistened or dried to optimum moisture content to
ensure proper compaction. The backfill material may be native material, but no
rock larger than ten inches (10") shall be allowed back into the trench or
excavation.
   D.   Approval Required Prior To Covering: No excavation project or activity
performed within the Town which affects Town streets, roadways or driveways
shall be covered over until authorized personnel from the Town have completed
an on site inspection and given approval of the work.
   E.   Repairs, Restoration: After backfilling activities have been completed
along right-of-ways, the party responsible shall thoroughly clean up and remove
all items and/or materials remaining as a result of the work. All fences,
culverts, lawns and other improvements which are damaged as a result of the
work, shall be repaired and restored to their original condition by the party
causing the damage.
   F.   Time Limit For Repair, Restoration: The repair and restoration work on
each and every project shall be done immediately following completion of the
project, on a continual basis. Maximum time for repairing and/or restoring the
disturbed area shall be fifteen (15) days, unless additional time is allowed by
the governing body of the Town.
   G.   Guarantee, Maintenance: It shall be the duty of the permittee to
guarantee and maintain the site of the excavation work in the same condition it
was prior to the excavation for two (2) years after restoring it to its
original condition.
(Ord. 178, 6-14-1993)
CHAPTER 3: TREE PROTECTION, ADMINISTRATION AND MANAGEMENT
Section
7-3-1: Tree Advisory Board
7-3-2: Definitions
7-3-3: Species To Be Planted
7-3-4: Spacing
7-3-5: Distance From Curb And Sidewalk
7-3-6: Distance From Street Corner, Fire Hydrants And Streetlights
7-3-7: Utilities
7-3-8: Public Tree Care
7-3-9: Tree Topping
7-3-10: Hazardous Tree Removal On Private Property
7-3-11: Tree Removal On Public Land
7-3-12: Exemption For Existing Trees
7-3-13: Penalty
7-3-1: TREE ADVISORY BOARD:
   A.   Creation And Establishment: There is hereby created and established a
Town Tree Advisory Board, which will consist of volunteer members at large,
subject to the approval of the Mayor and Town Council. This board will also be
known as the Beautification Committee.
   B.   Compensation: At large members of the board shall serve without
compensation.
   C.   Duties And Responsibilities:
      1.   It shall be the responsibility of the Tree Advisory Board to study,
investigate, counsel and develop written standards, rules and regulations for
the care, preservation, trimming, planting, replanting, removal or disposition
of trees and shrubs in public ways, streets and alleys. Such standards will be
presented to the Town Council and upon their acceptance and approval shall
constitute amendments to the official Town tree ordinance and shall constitute
the official comprehensive Town Tree Plan for the Town.
      2.   The Tree Advisory Board, when requested by the Town Council, shall
consider, investigate, make findings, report and recommend upon any special
matter of question coming within the scope of its responsibilities.
   D.   Organization: The Tree Advisory Board shall choose its own officers,
make its own rules and regulations and keep a journal of its proceedings. A
majority of the members shall be a quorum for the transaction of business.
   E.   Town Council Approval Of Rules And Regulations: The Town may, and it
hereby expressly reserves the right, at any time or times, to adopt new rules
or regulations to amend, alter and/or repeal any rule, regulation and/or
article, section, paragraph and/or sentence in these rules and regulations.
   F.   Review By Council; Appeals: The Town Council shall have the right to
review the conduct, acts and decisions of the Tree Advisory Board. Any person
may appeal from any ruling or order of the Tree Advisor Board to the Town
Council, who may hear the matter and make final decisions.
   G.   Provide Advice: The Tree Advisory Board will provide, upon request,
information and advice concerning tree species selection, care and planting of
trees and other related information.
   H.   Interference With Board: It shall be unlawful for any person to
prevent, delay or interfere with the Tree Advisory Board, or any other of their
agents or servants, while engaging in planting, cultivating, mulching, pruning,
spraying or removing of any street trees or trees on private grounds, as
authorized by this chapter.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases used in this chapter shall have the following
meanings unless a different meaning clearly appears from the context:
STREET TREES: Trees on Town property lying between private property lines on
either side of all streets, avenues or ways within the Town.
TREE: Any self-supporting woody plant, together with its root system growing
upon the earth usually with one trunk of at least one inch (1") in diameter at
a height of four and one-half feet (41/2') above the ground, or a multi-stemmed
trunk system with a definitely formed crown.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-3: SPECIES TO BE PLANTED:
Any trees which are hardy and adaptable to this altitude zone and recommended
for growth in this area may be planted. Listings of trees recommended for
growth in Wyoming are available from the Tree Advisory Board, the Agricultural
Extension Service, University of Wyoming, Laramie, Wyoming, local master
gardeners or from the local County Extension Service.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-4: SPACING:
The spacing of street trees will be in accordance with the recommendations of
the Agricultural Extension Service, University of Wyoming, or from the local
County Extension Agent for the particular type of tree to be planted.
Consideration shall be given for special plantings designed or approved by a
landscape architect, landscape designer or person engaged in the field of
landscape contracting.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-5: DISTANCE FROM CURB AND SIDEWALK:
The distance trees may be planted from curbs or curblines and sidewalks will be
in accordance with species and size of tree to be planted. No trees may be
planted closer to any curb or sidewalk than the following, unless the use of a
root barrier is used:
 
Small tree:  Two feet (2')
Medium tree: Three feet (3')
Large tree:  Four feet (4')
 
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-6: DISTANCE FROM STREET CORNER, FIRE HYDRANTS AND STREETLIGHTS:
No street tree shall be planted closer than thirty feet (30') of any street
corner, measured from the point of nearest intersecting curbs or curb lines. No
street tree shall be planted closer than ten feet (10') of any fire hydrant or
streetlight.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-7: UTILITIES:
The Tree Advisory Board recommends that no street trees be planted under or
within ten (10) lateral feet of any overhead utility wire, or over or within
five (5) lateral feet of any underground water line, sewer line, transmission
line or other utility.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-8: PUBLIC TREE CARE:
The Town shall have the right, but does not have the obligation, to plant,
prune, spray, preserve and remove within the lines of all streets, alleys,
avenues, lanes, squares and public grounds as may be necessary to ensure public
safety or to preserve the symmetry and beauty of such public grounds. The Tree
Advisory Board may remove or cause or order to be removed any tree or part
thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which by reason of its nature is
injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines, other public
improvements, or is affected by any fungus, insect or other pest.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-9: TREE TOPPING:
It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any person, firm or Town
department to top any street tree, or other tree on public property. Topping is
defined as the severe cutting back of limbs to stubs larger than three inches
(3") in diameter with the tree’s crown to such a degree so as to remove the
normal canopy or disfigure the tree. Trees severely damaged by storms or other
causes or certain trees under utility wires or other obstructions where other
pruning practices are impractical may be exempted from this section at the
determination of the Tree Advisory Board.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-10: HAZARDOUS TREE REMOVAL ON PRIVATE PROPERTY:
The Town shall have the right to cause the removal of any dead or diseased
trees on private property within the Town, when such trees constitute a hazard
to life and property, or harbor insects or disease which constitute a potential
threat to other trees within the Town. The Tree Advisory Board will notify in
writing the owners of such trees. Removal shall be done by said owners at their
expense within sixty (60) days after the date of service notice. In the event
of failure of owners to comply with such provisions, the Town shall have the
authority to remove such trees and charge the cost of removal to the owners.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-11: TREE REMOVAL ON PUBLIC LAND:
A.   Permit Required: It shall be unlawful for any person, either for himself
or another, to remove, destroy or cause to be destroyed any tree in or upon
public right-of-way of any street, alley, sidewalk or other public place within
the Town, without having first obtained a written permit thereof. Any person
desiring a permit to remove a tree, as required by this section, shall submit a
written application to the Town Tree Advisory Board for each tree or groups of
trees per location. Such application shall be set forth the name and address of
the applicant and owner, the name and address of the person doing the work, the
kind of species of tree to be removed, location, of the tree, purpose of tree
removal and landscape or site plan if possible.
B.   Replacement Tree Required: A removal permit will be granted with the
agreement that a replacement tree will be planted in its place, or in a close
adjacent location as in accordance by this chapter.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-12: EXEMPTION FOR EXISTING TREES:
Trees already in place and growing at the date of adoption of this chapter
shall be exempt from sections
7-3-3 through
7-3-6 of this chapter. However, any replacement trees shall be governed by
these sections.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
7-3-13: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter or who fails to comply with
any notice issued pursuant to provisions of this chapter, upon being found
guilty of violation, shall be subject to section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 205, 2-9-1998)
CHAPTER 4: RIGHT-OF-WAY PERMITS
Section
   
7-4-1: General
   
7-4-2: Application
   
7-4-3: Review And Issuance
   
7-4-4: Inspection
   
7-4-5: Completion
   
7-4-6: Emergency Repair
   
7-4-7: Warranty
   
7-4-8: Site Conditions And Permittee Responsibilities
 
   
7-4-9: Penalty
7-4-1: GENERAL:
   A.   Without obtaining a right of way permit from the Town of Thayne, it is
unlawful for any person to:
      1.   Construct infrastructure such as, but not limited to, sidewalk,
boardwalk, curbs, gutters, and street paving within any street.
      2.   Dig up, break, excavate, tunnel, undermine, or in any manner break
up any street, or to make or cause to be made any excavation in or under the
surface of any street for any purpose.
      3.   Place, deposit, or leave upon any street any earth or other
excavated material obstructing or tending to interfere with the free use of the
street, or
      4.   Move an existing house, building, or structure on or over any street
for the purpose of construction, excavation, tunneling, or storage of materials
or for activities which would facilitate such.
   B.   No dig periods. No right of way permit shall be issued starting
November 1st through May 1st of each calendar year, except by special
permission of the Town. The May 1st date may be extended or shortened at the
election of the Town Council.
   C.   All right-of-way excavation work shall comply with Town specifications.
   D.   Unless otherwise approved by the Town, fiber communications facilities,
gas facilities and electric facilities shall be buried as per subject utility
specifications and drawings.
   E.   The provisions of this article shall not be applicable to any
excavation work under the direction of Town authorities, by employees of the
Town or by any contractor of the Town performing work for and on behalf of the
Town necessitating openings or excavations in streets.
   F.   The provisions of this article shall be applicable to all persons
operating public utilities in the Town under franchises granted by the Town and
having the right, either by general or special permission, to enter upon
streets and open and excavate pavements, sidewalks or disturb the surface
thereof by excavation or other work, and such persons shall be required to
apply for a permit and to comply with all other provisions of this article.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-4-2: APPLICATION:
   A.   The application shall include emergency contact information, dates of
work, construction plans, work schedule, traffic control plan, necessary
encroachment agreements.
   B.   The Town reserves the right to require the construction plans to be
prepared by a Wyoming licensed professional engineer.
   C.   Proof of liability insurance from the contractor doing work within the
right-of-way and an additional insured status of its operations and/or
employees, vehicles, equipment and actions, and a signed indemnification
agreement further indemnifying the Town of all liability created out of the
actions of the subject contractor on the subject work.
   D.   General liability to cover public and private property damage; hold
harmless form. Liability insurance shall be maintained in an amount not less
than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for damages per occurrence and in the
amount not less than two million dollars ($2,000,000.00) in the aggregate. The
Town may require a certificate of insurance and an additional insured status
with a waiver of subrogation.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-4-3: REVIEW AND ISSUANCE:
   A.   The application shall be submitted no more than four weeks prior to the
start of construction unless prior approval is granted by the Town to submit it
earlier.
   B.   Length of time for application review is dependent upon the size and
complexity of the work to be done within the Town right-of-way.
   C.   A permit shall not be assigned or transferred without the written
consent of the Town.
   D.   The permittee shall maintain an on-site copy of the approved permit,
plans, and specifications.
7-4-4: INSPECTION:
   A.   All inspections shall have forty-eight-hour notice to the Town for
inspection calls. Weekend and after-hours inspections may be arranged if Town
staffing allows. All after-hours inspections will be billed in advance at a
rate established by Town Council.
   B.   Town staff shall make such inspections as are reasonably necessary in
the enforcement of this article.
   C.   The Town reserves the right to require a third-party engineer to
conduct inspections, at the expense of the permittee. Third-party inspectors
must be preapproved by the Town.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-4-5: COMPLETION:
   A.   The permittee shall prosecute and complete all work covered by the
right-of way permit and shall restore the street to its original condition not
later than the date specified in the right-of-way permit.
   B.   Unless waived by the Town, a person designated by the permittee shall
provide the Town a certificate of completion stating the date for the work
performed (Including restoration), identifying the installer, the location at
which the work was performed, and certifying that work was completed according
to the requirements of the Town. If a utility or contractor has one outstanding
certificate, the Town reserves the right to withhold issuing future permits
until the certificates are submitted. The Town shall conduct an inspection
before the as-builts are submitted.
   C.   If necessary, the permittee shall submit “as built” drawings, maps,
and/or underground structure maintenance drawings after construction. The Town
can require a facility to be removed at the owner’s expense from a right-of-way
if it is in a nonpermitted location.
   D.   Extension required. No person may excavate or obstruct the right-of-way
after the completion date specified on the permit unless the person obtains an
extension prior to the completion date or obtains a new permit.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-4-6: EMERGENCY REPAIR:
In the event of any emergency in which a main, conduit or utility in or under
any street breaks, bursts or otherwise is in such condition as to immediately
endanger the property, life, health or safety of any individual, the person
owning or controlling such main, conduit or utility, without first applying for
and obtaining a right-of-way permit hereunder, shall immediately take proper
emergency measures to cure or remedy the dangerous conditions for the
protection of property, life, health and safety of individuals. The applicant
shall notify the Town as soon as possible of the event. Within two business
days after the occurrence of the emergency, the applicant shall apply for the
necessary permits, pay the fees associated therewith, and fulfill the rest of
the requirements necessary to bring itself into compliance with the permit
requirements for the actions it took in response to the emergency. If a utility
is damaged and repaired within the excavation made by the primary permit
holder, an additional permit is not required; however, notification to the Town
is still required.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-4-7: WARRANTY:
   A.   All excavations will have to be guaranteed from deterioration for a
period of one year. If patch failure occurs, as determined by the Town, repair
will be made as per specified by the Town. After the repair, the excavation
shall be guaranteed for an additional one-year period.
   B.   From the issued date of the certificate of completion to one year, the
applicant will be responsible for all unsatisfactory conditions of subsidence,
asphalt repairs, poor drainage, vegetation, and Town-owned utilities that have
been disturbed, cut into or patched as a result of the subject work. Upon the
one-year anniversary date, the applicant will be notified, and the financial
guarantee returned.
   C.   Release of financial guarantee. No release of the financial guarantee
shall take place without the prior approval of the Town and after a physical
inspection by the Town.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-7-8: SITE CONDITIONS AND PERMITTEE RESPONSIBILITIES:
The permittee is responsible and shall bear all costs associated with
maintaining and restoring the site conditions.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
7-7-9: PENALTY:
Any person, partnership, corporation or legal entity who violates any provision
of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punished in accordance with section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such
under this chapter.
(Ord. 393, - -2024)
CHAPTER 5: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
7-5-1: Parking In Town Parking Lots
   
7-5-2: Parking During Winter Months
 
   
7-5-3: Penalty
7-5-1: PARKING IN TOWN PARKING LOTS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to park any motor vehicle, mobile home, motor
home, house trailer or similar vehicle in any town parking lot for longer than
twenty-four consecutive hours or between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m.
of every day.
   B.   It shall be unlawful to park or store any tractor, tractor trailer,
farm machinery or other equipment, other than as provided in subsection (a)
hereof, on any Town parking lot for any period of time at all.
(Ord. 394, - -2024)
7-5-2: PARKING DURING WINTER MONTHS:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this section, the word “vehicle” shall
mean any device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a street or highway, including, but not limited to,
motor vehicles and trailers.
   B.   Time Period Parking Is Prohibited: Parking is prohibited on any town
street, town right-of-way, or town parking lot from two o’clock (2:00) A.M. to
six o’clock (6:00) A.M. from November 1 to March 31.
   C.   Removal By Town: In case any vehicles are parked or left standing on
any town street, town right-of-way, or town parking lot in violation of this
section, said vehicle or vehicles may be removed by or under the direction of
any police officer or town employee. Removal of the vehicle by or under the
direction of a police officer or town employee shall not prevent prosecution
under this section. Within seventy-two (72) hours from the time of removal of
any vehicle, notice of the removal or impounding, or both, together with the
designation of the pound, shall be given by the police officer or town employee
to the owner of record of such vehicle. Such notice may be made in person or by
telephone, when possible, and if not possible, by letter.
(Ord. 394, - -2024)
7-5-3: PENALTY:
Any person, partnership, corporation, or legal entity who violates any
provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction
thereof, shall be punished in accordance with section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such
under this chapter.
(Ord. 394, - -2024)
TITLE 8: PUBLIC UTILITIES

CHAPTER 1: WATER USE AND SERVICE
Section
8-1-1: Reservation Of Rights
8-1-2: Management And Control Of Water System
8-1-3: Superintendent Of Water System
8-1-4: Connection; How Obtained; Connection Fees
8-1-5: New Developments And Nonresident Connection Fees
8-1-6: Permit Issuance
8-1-7: Connection Sizing
8-1-8: Water Meters
8-1-9: Service Pipe And Fittings
8-1-10: Required Depth
8-1-11: Connection Inspection And Approval
8-1-12: Connection Costs
8-1-13: Maintenance
8-1-14: Unauthorized Use Of Water
8-1-15: Town Not Liable For Damages
8-1-16: Inspection Of Property
8-1-17: Extension To More Than One Property
8-1-18: Proclamation Of Limited Use
8-1-19: User Charges
8-1-20: Frozen Water Service
8-1-21: Bills; When Due; Delinquency
8-1-22: Shutting Off Water
8-1-23: Restoration Following Voluntary Disconnection
8-1-24: Tampering With Water System
8-1-25: Unauthorized Turning On Of Water
8-1-26: Responsibility Of Balance Due
8-1-27: Penalty For Violations
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-1-103(a)(xxx)
8-1-1: RESERVATION OF RIGHTS:
The use of water under the provisions of this chapter shall not be deemed to be
a relinquishment of any water or water right by the Town and the Town reserves
the full right to determine all matters in connection with the control and use
of such water.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-2: MANAGEMENT AND CONTROL OF WATER SYSTEM:
The Town shall have exclusive control and management of the Town water system,
and shall have the exclusive management and control of the supply and
distribution of water to all users within and without the corporate limits, and
shall make such rules and regulations as are necessary for the management,
control, distribution and supply of water to the users of the system.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-3: SUPERINTENDENT OF WATER SYSTEM:
The Mayor, with the advice and consent of the Town Council, shall appoint a
superintendent of the Town water system, who shall have immediate charge, under
the direction of the Mayor and Town Council, of such system, and of connections
to the system, alterations or additions to the system, and shall have
supervision of such system.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-4: CONNECTION; HOW OBTAINED; CONNECTION FEES:
   A.   Application; Fees: Any person desiring to obtain a supply of water from
the Town water system shall submit an application to the Town Clerk. The
application is available at Town Hall or on the Town website. If any easements
are required in order for the applicant to connect to the Town water system,
the applicant shall supply such easement in written form, duly acknowledged,
along with the application. The fees for connection to the Town water system
shall be based upon the size of the pipe required for the service line running
from the City water main to the property of the applicant for the following
pipe sizes (meter size shall match the size of the service line running to the
property line).
 
Size Of Service Line            Impact Fee       Connection Fee
3/4 inch                        $6,800.00        $500.00
1 inch                          10,200.00        500.00
2 inch                          20,400.00        500.00
Fire line connection (up to 4") To be determined 500.00
                                by Council
 
   B.   Service Line Fees: Residential fees for service lines which fall
between and above the listed connection sizes shall be determined by the Town
Council.
   C.   Fire Suppression Systems: Buildings designed with fire suppression
systems shall have a separate connection and shall pay a standard connection
fee for lines up to four inches (4"). Fees for fire connections above four
inches (4") shall be determined by the Town Council.
   D.   When Fees Due: For applicants applying for water service to an existing
lot, both the impact fee and the connection fee are due at the time of
application. The connection fee shall be paid at the time of application for
water service to a lot. (Ord. 275; amd. Ord. 386, - -2023)
8-1-5: NEW DEVELOPMENTS AND NONRESIDENT CONNECTION FEES:
Impact fees and connection fees shall be one hundred twenty five percent (125%)
for new users outside of Town limits.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-6: PERMIT ISSUANCE:
If the Town Clerk determines that the application is complete, the Town Clerk
shall issue a permit for connection to the Town water system. When connection
has been completed in compliance with the provisions of this chapter, the
superintendent or owner shall provide the information regarding the connection
as specified on the permit and shall return the permit to the Town Clerk within
twenty four (24) hours after the completion of the connections. All such
completed permits shall be kept on file in the Office of the Town Clerk.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-7: CONNECTION SIZING:
The water service tap, service line and meter size shall be three-fourths inch
(3/4") for residences unless otherwise dictated by the latest edition of the
International Plumbing Code and approved by the Town. Service sizes for
commercial connections and multiple living units shall be sized in accordance
with the latest edition of the International Plumbing Code and approved by the
Town.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-8: WATER METERS:
   A.   Required; Owner Responsible For Cost: All connections to the Town water
system shall be metered with the exception of connections used exclusively for
fire suppression systems within buildings. Meter assemblies, including the
meter, radio, meter pit, setter, and service saddle shall be obtained from the
Town. The owner shall pay the actual cost of all equipment supplied by the
Town. Equipment costs are in addition to the connection fee paid by the owner.
   B.   Location; Installation: Meters shall be located at the property line at
a location approved by the Water Superintendent. If it is impractical to locate
the meter on the property line, the meter may be installed at a location
mutually agreed upon by the user and Water Superintendent and approved by the
Town Council. Should the meter be located on private property, the user and
Town shall sign an agreement allowing Town personnel access to the meter.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-9: SERVICE PIPE AND FITTINGS:
All service pipe shall be polyethylene conforming to the requirements of AWWA
C-901. Pipe shall be a pressure tubing class 160 with a DR of 11 at a minimum.
All fittings including service saddle, corporation stops, and compression
connections shall be copper alloy and shall be approved by the Water
Superintendent.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-10: REQUIRED DEPTH:
All service lines shall be laid six feet (6') below the established grade at
the point of connection of the service line onto the Town water line. Where the
Town line is of greater or less depth, the service line shall be brought to the
required depth as soon as possible after leaving the tap.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-11: CONNECTION INSPECTION AND APPROVAL:
No person except a licensed plumber, or a contractor who is authorized, in
writing, by the Water Superintendent, shall tap or connect onto any water pipes
belonging to the Town. Any damage to a Town water pipe that is caused by a
person performing a tap shall be repaired at the expense of the person
performing the tap. No street shall be opened or water pipe tapped or service
pipe laid unless the Water Superintendent has been notified in advance of such
action. All work pertaining to the connection onto the Town water system shall
be done in accordance with the directions of the Water Superintendent. No
excavation related to connection onto the water system shall be filled in until
the work has been inspected and approved by the Water Superintendent.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-12: CONNECTION COSTS:
The service line from the Town water main to the user's premises, including the
water meter assembly (meter box, setter and associated fittings), shall be
installed by the user at the user's sole cost.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-13: MAINTENANCE:
The owner of any property shall keep the service line and other equipment
related to the supply of water to such person's property in good working order
and repair.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-14: UNAUTHORIZED USE OF WATER:
If any water consumer shall permit any other person from other premises or any
unauthorized person to use or obtain water from such consumer's property, the
supply of water of such consumer may be terminated. Any unauthorized person
taking water from another's property is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be subject to section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-15: TOWN NOT LIABLE FOR DAMAGES:
The Town shall not be liable to the users of any water for interruptions of
water supply, scarcity of water, accidents to the system or any part thereof,
or damage from frost, electrolysis, or any unavoidable causes.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-16: INSPECTION OF PROPERTY:
Free access shall be allowed at all reasonable hours to the Water
Superintendent, or to any other authorized person, to all places supplied with
water from the Town water system, to examine the amount of water used, the
manner of its use to obtain a test sample, or to ascertain any matter
pertaining to the use of water from the Town water system and the charges made
thereof.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-17: EXTENSION TO MORE THAN ONE PROPERTY:
Unless otherwise authorized by the Town Council, each property shall be
supplied water by its own service line, and no connection with the water system
shall be made by extending the service line from one property to another
property.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-18: PROCLAMATION OF LIMITED USE:
   A.   Authorized: In time of scarcity or when the system is unable to supply
a sufficient amount of water for all purposes, the Mayor by proclamation may
limit the use of water for other than domestic purposes to such extent as may
be necessary for the public health, safety and general welfare.
   B.   Penalty: If, after the Mayor has issued a proclamation regulating the
use of water, any person or persons, by himself or through his family, servant
or agent, violates the provisions of such proclamation, person or persons will
be such guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be subject to section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-19: USER CHARGES:
   A.   Basic Charge: The basic charge for use of water from the Town water
system shall be thirty four dollars seventy five cents ($34.75) per month,
which shall be adjusted to the number of equivalent connections utilized by
each user on the system, minimum being one. Each paid equivalent connection is
entitled to use up to thirty thousand (30,000) gallons in a given month when
water usage is metered. One bill will be sent per meter regardless of
equivalent connections.
   B.   Excess Of Base Volume: All water used in excess of the base volume by
any connection in a month, when metered, will be charged one dollar fifty cents
($1.50) per one thousand (1,000) gallons. The Town will not charge for water
used above the base amount of thirty thousand (30,000) gallons per month from
the first business day of November to the first business day of May to
encourage users to leave a small stream of water running to prevent freezing of
service lines.
   C.   Classifications, Equivalent Connections: Users shall have the following
classifications and equivalent connections:
Water Classification Number of Equivalent Connections
Water Classification                          Number of Equivalent Connections
Single-family residence (¾" tap and meter)   1
Single-family residence (1" tap and meter)    1.5
Per apartment/condominium/duplex/town home    1
Bank                                          1
Bar/club/tavern/saloon                        1
Barber shop/beauty saloon (per chair/operator .5
station)
Bowling alley (per lane)                      .2
Cafe/restaurant                               2
Car dealer                                    2
Car wash                                      3
Church                                        2
Dry cleaners                                  1
Garage/service station                        1
Hospital (per bed)                            .15
Laundries/laundry mater (per washing machine) .25
Meat processing plant                         1.5
Mobile/food truck                             .5
Mobile home court or park (per space)         1
Motel/hotel                                   Main lodge 1
                                              Each additional room .25
Office building/retail store                  1
Grocery stores/retail food store (per 2,5000  1
square feet)
Schools                                       2
Swimming pools                                1
Theater                                       1
 
   D.   Larger Meters; Uses Not Listed: The Town shall determine equivalent
connections for any residence requiring a service and meter larger than one
inch (1") and any other use not listed above, at the time of approval of an
application for connection to the Town water system.
   E.   Users Outside Town: When water service is provided to users outside the
Town limits, the rate shall be one hundred twenty five percent (125%) of the
regular basic user charges, which shall be adjusted to the number of equivalent
connections utilized by each user on the system. Each paid equivalent
connection is entitled to use up to thirty thousand (30,000) gallons in a given
month when water usage is metered.
(Ord. 321, 6-15-2017; amd. Ord. 338, 4-29-2019; Ord. 386, - -2023)
8-1-20: FROZEN WATER SERVICE:
The Town is not responsible for the cost of repairing or thawing of water
service lines. The entire water service line from the main line to the user's
point of use is the responsibility of the property owner. Water users are
responsible for all freeze damage and service interruption due to service line
freezing. Water meter damage from freezing will be repaired at the user's
expense.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-21: BILLS; WHEN DUE; DELINQUENCY:
All bills for water service are payable monthly and are due on the last
business day of the month. A late payment penalty of ten dollars ($10.00) will
be assessed each billing cycle on accounts that are delinquent. Interest will
be charged on delinquent accounts at the rate of one and one-half percent (11/
2%), compounded, for each full billing period or portion of a billing period
that the account is delinquent. Account will be considered delinquent if
payment has not been received by five o'clock (5:00) P.M. of the last business
day of the billing month, and a reasonable attorney fee for collection of the
same may be recovered by the Town. Any exception will require Council approval.
(Ord. 321, 6-15-2017)
8-1-22: SHUTTING OFF WATER:
   A.   Authorized: Water service may be shut off when water use charges for
any property have been delinquent and unpaid for more than two (2) months. The
Water Superintendent shall have the authority to shut off the water from the
property until such delinquent charges, together with such other costs as may
have accrued, shall have been paid in full.
   B.   Notice Not Required: Notice shall not be required to the owner, lessee
or any occupant of the property before shutting off such water, and this
subsection shall be deemed notice to all persons interested that water supplied
to any property may be shut off unless charges for such water are paid before
the same becomes delinquent.
   C.   Charges: When charges for water are unpaid, or for any other reason due
to the violation of the provisions of this chapter, or any rules or regulations
adopted hereunder, the water supply to any property is shut off, before the
same is again turned on, the Water Superintendent or the Town Clerk shall
charge and collect, in addition to all delinquent water use charges, a fee of
fifty dollars ($50.00) for turning on such water service.
   D.   Restoration Of Water Service: When account balance is paid in full and
all fees have been paid, the water will be turned back on within 48 hours
unless payment is received on a Friday and as such the 48 hours will not start
until the following business day.
(Ord. 275; amd. Ord. 386, - -2023)
8-1-23: RESTORATION FOLLOWING VOLUNTARY DISCONNECTION:
When water service is disconnected to a water user at the request of such user,
the Water Superintendent or the Town Clerk shall charge a vacation rate of
fifteen dollars ($15.00) per month per equivalent connection while during such
time that service is disconnected. The consumer shall be charged a reconnection
fee of thirty five dollars ($35.00). User charges applicable to restored water
service shall be prorated from the first day of the month in which the water
service is restored.
(Ord. 295, 9-19-2013)
8-1-24: TAMPERING WITH WATER SYSTEM:
Any person not acting in an official capacity as a representative of the Town
or the Fire Department who shall open any hydrant and allow water to escape
thereof, or shall in any manner interfere with or damage the Town water system
or any portion thereof, or shall turn off or on any water service without the
approval of the Water Superintendent, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and,
upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-25: UNAUTHORIZED TURNING ON OF WATER:
Any person whose water service has been terminated or shut off due to
nonpayment of user charges or for any other reason turns the water on, or
permits the water to be turned on, or uses or permits the water to be used
without authorization from the Town, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(Ord. 275)
8-1-26: RESPONSIBILITY OF BALANCE DUE:
Regardless of if a water bill is received or not the user is responsible for
the balance due.
(Ord. 386, - -2023)
8-1-27: PENALTY FOR VIOLATIONS:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter is guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, except in cases where a specific
penalty is pervaded, shall be subject to section
1-4-1 of this Code.
(Ord. 275; amd. Ord. 386, - -2023)
CHAPTER 2: SEWAGE TREATMENT AND REGULATIONS
ARTICLE A. GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section
8-2A-1: Definitions
8-2A-2: Ownership, Management And Control Of Sewage Treatment System
8-2A-3: Commissioner Of Sewage Treatment System
8-2A-4: Authority To Classify Property And Modify Rates
8-2A-5: Adoption Of Additional Rules And Regulations
8-2A-6: Power And Duties Of Administrative Officials
8-2A-7: Permit Required For Alteration Of Service Line
8-2A-8: Separate Service Line Required For Each Property; Plumbing Fixtures To
Be Connected By Property Owner Upon Notice
8-2A-9: Sand And Grease Traps Required For Establishments Having Wash Or Grease
Racks
8-2A-10: Depositing Injurious Material Into System
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-1-103(a)(xxx)
8-2A-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section:
SEWER SERVICE LINE: The sewer line running from the Municipal sewer main to the
structure or property to be served.
SEWER UTILITY: All sanitary sewers, sewage treatment works, equipment,
materials and supplies used by the Municipality to collect and dispose of
sewage from property in the Municipality and property served by Municipal
sewers outside the Municipality; provided, that a sewer service line shall be
regarded as the property of the owner of such structure or property served.
(1982 Code § 12.01.010)
8-2A-2: OWNERSHIP, MANAGEMENT AND CONTROL OF SEWAGE TREATMENT SYSTEM:
The sewage treatment system of the Town shall be owned, maintained, controlled
and managed exclusively by the Town, and through such agents and
representatives as are duly appointed by the Mayor and Town Council.
(1982 Code § 12.01.020)
8-2A-3: COMMISSIONER OF SEWAGE TREATMENT SYSTEM:
The commissioner of the sewage treatment system shall be the Sewer and Water
Commissioner of the Town, who shall be appointed by and have such powers and
duties as prescribed by the Town Council.
(1982 Code § 12.01.030)
8-2A-4: AUTHORITY TO CLASSIFY PROPERTY AND MODIFY RATES:
The Town Council shall have the right to determine, define and classify all
residences, businesses and other properties, and to increase, modify or revise
by ordinance the rates and charges established for the provision of sewer
utility services to such properties.
(1982 Code § 12.01.040)
8-2A-5: ADOPTION OF ADDITIONAL RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The Town may, from time to time, promulgate such rules and regulations as it
considers necessary to carry out the intent of this chapter; provided, that
such rules and regulations shall not be inconsistent with this chapter.
(1982 Code § 12.01.050)
8-2A-6: POWER AND DUTIES OF ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICIALS:
The Town shall cause to be inspected all openings made in any sewer and all
connections made to the sewer utility. It shall take such action as it deems
necessary to prevent injury or damage to the sewer utility and to prevent
interference with the free flow of sewage.
(1982 Code § 12.01.060)
8-2A-7: PERMIT REQUIRED FOR ALTERATION OF SERVICE LINE:
It shall be unlawful to extend any sewer service line or to change, enlarge or
alter the use of any sewer service line connected to the sewer utility without
first obtaining a permit therefor. No such permit shall be issued to property
situated outside the Municipality, except under such terms and conditions as
the governing body shall provide.
(1982 Code § 12.01.070)
8-2A-8: SEPARATE SERVICE LINE REQUIRED FOR EACH PROPERTY; PLUMBING FIXTURES TO
BE CONNECTED BY PROPERTY OWNER UPON NOTICE:
Each property shall be served by its own sewer service line. All plumbing
fixtures in any building or structure on and land adjoining to or abutting on
or near any street or alley or other place through which there is a public or
private sewer connected with the sanitary sewer utility of the Municipality
shall be connected by the owner of the property or his agent or other persons
having charge of or receiving the rent or being the tenant of the same, with
such public or private sewer upon notice from the Municipality. Such notice
shall be served upon the owner of such property by registered or certified mail
to his last known address; provided, that this section shall not be construed
as prohibiting a single service line to serve a single structure under one roof
occupying more than one property.
(1982 Code § 12.01.080)
8-2A-9: SAND AND GREASE TRAPS REQUIRED FOR ESTABLISHMENTS HAVING WASH OR GREASE
RACKS:
All filling stations, garages, restaurants and similar places having wash or
grease racks connected with the sewer utility shall be provided with a sand and
grease trap of suitable sizes and construction.
(1982 Code § 12.01.090)
8-2A-10: DEPOSITING INJURIOUS MATERIAL INTO SYSTEM:
It shall be unlawful to throw or deposit or cause or permit to be deposited in
any vessel or receptacle connected with the sewer utility any petroleum
products, volatiles, acids, highly alkaline solutions or any other matter
whatsoever, which shall in any way be injurious to the system or the treatment
process at the treatment plant, or which shall in any way cause undue
maintenance of the system or the sewage plant.
(1982 Code § 12.01.100)
ARTICLE B. SEWER CONNECTIONS
Section
8-2B-1: Connection Required; Exceptions
8-2B-2: Connections Made Before Paving Adjacent Street
8-2B-3: Permit Required
8-2B-4: Application For Permit
8-2B-5: Contents; Fees
8-2B-6: Types Of Permits Issued
8-2B-7: Plumbing Inspected Before Connections Made
8-2B-8: Connection Of Water Drains, Downspouts, Etc.
8-2B-9: Connection Fee For Sewer Service
8-2B-1: CONNECTION REQUIRED; EXCEPTIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain any cesspool, septic tank,
privy or other private sewer system whatsoever to service any sewer user within
the corporate limits of the Town if such user has reasonable or practical
access to the Town sewer system. It is hereby required that each and every
sewer user within the corporate limits of the Town having reasonable or
practical access to the Town sewer system shall connect onto the Town sewer
system and utilize the same. Any sewer user in violation of this section shall
be subject to provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code, and shall also be billed for a monthly sewer user's fee
according to the sewer user’s classification for such user as of the date when
water was first supplied to the user’s property.
(1982 Code § 12.02.010)
8-2B-2: CONNECTIONS MADE BEFORE PAVING ADJACENT STREET:
Before any street or alley is paved, the owners of all property abutting
thereon where a sanitary sewer is laid shall make property sewer connections
with such sanitary sewer, whether the immediate use thereof is required or not.
Until used, such connecting sewers shall be supplied with a proper cap or
covering sufficient to prevent the escape of sewer gas.
(1982 Code § 12.02.020)
8-2B-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall make any connection to or uncover or open any Municipal sewer
without first obtaining a permit therefor from the Town Clerk.
(1982 Code § 12.02.030)
8-2B-4: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Any person desiring to make any connection to the sewer utility shall make
written application to the Town Clerk for a permit. All such applications must
contain a description of the property to be connected, the kind and sizes of
the service line and the kinds of fixtures to be served.
(1982 Code § 12.02.040)
8-2B-5: CONTENTS; FEES:
The permit shall state the name and address of the person making the connection
or excavation, the property to be served, the location of the tap to the
Municipal sewer main and the size of the tap. No permit shall be issued unless
the fees prescribed by the Municipality are tendered with the application for a
permit. Such fees shall be as are established from time to time by the
governing body.
(1982 Code § 12.02.050)
8-2B-6: TYPES OF PERMIT ISSUED:
The following types of permits shall be issued for connecting to the sewer
utility:
A.   Permits to run a sewer service line from the sewer main to the property
line of the property to be served.
B.   Permits to run a sewer service line from the sewer main to the structure
or building to be served.
C.   Permits to run a sewer from the stubbed-in service at the property line to
the building or other structure to be served.
D.   Permits to connect a sewer service line to the sewer utility to serve
property outside the Municipality; provided, that no permit shall be issued to
connect with the sewer utility to serve property lying outside the Municipality
except with the express consent of the governing body and under such terms and
conditions as the governing body may by resolution prescribe.
E.   Permits to renew any of the sewer service lines provided for in this
section.
(1982 Code § 12.02.060)
8-2B-7: PLUMBING INSPECTED BEFORE CONNECTIONS MADE:
All plumbing shall be subject to inspection by the Town or its authorized
representatives, in order to ascertain whether the requirements of this chapter
have been or are being complied with. It shall be unlawful for any person to
cause any plumbing within or outside the Municipality to be connected with the
sewer utility of the Municipality until such plumbing shall have been inspected
and approved and a certificate or tag of approval issued by the Municipality.
(1982 Code § 12.02.070)
8-2B-8: CONNECTION OF WATER DRAINS, DOWNSPOUTS, ETC.:
It shall be unlawful to connect any storm water drains, downspouts, subsurface
drainage system or steam exhausts or blowoff from a steam boiler to the
sanitary system.
(1982 Code § 2.02.080)
8-2B-9: CONNECTION FEE FOR SEWER SERVICE:
A new sewer user, upon application for water and sewer service, shall pay in
advance the connection fees as established by the Town Council from time to
time.
(1982 Code § 12.02.090)
ARTICLE C. INSTALLATION AND REPAIR OF SYSTEM
Section
8-2C-1: Service Lines
8-2C-2: Backfilling Of Trenches
8-2C-3: Maintenance Of Inside Of Service Lines
8-2C-4: Property Owner Responsible For Cost Of Installing, Repairing Service
Lines
8-2C-5: Method And Specifications For Making Connections To Sewer Mains
8-2C-6: Construction Of Sewers In Subdivisions
8-2C-7: Extension Of Sewer To Serve Property Within Municipality Not Part Of
Subdivision
8-2C-8: Nongravity Lines
8-2C-9: Extension Of Service Outside Municipality
8-2C-1: SERVICE LINES:
   A.   Requirements Of Installation: All pipe used in making any sewer tap or
installation or connection shall be standard approved sewer pipe or polyvinyl
chloride pipe (PVC) not less than four inches (4") in diameter. The pipe and
fittings used for the sewer system lines shall conform to the following
applicable specifications:
      1.   Fittings: The pipe and fittings shall be bell and spigot, sealed
with rubber gasket joining material. Rubber gaskets shall conform to the
requirements of ASTM Specification C-564.
      2.   Nonreinforced Concrete Sewer Pipe: Nonreinforced concrete sewer pipe
shall be either standard strength or extra strength. Concrete pipe shall
conform to the requirements of ASTM Specification C-14. The pipe shall be bell
and spigot type, sealing by means of flexible, watertight rubber gaskets. The
joints and gasket material shall conform to the requirements of ASTM
Specification C-443.
      3.   Plastic Sewer Pipe And Fittings (For Nonpressure System): Plastic
sewer pipe shall be, unless otherwise indicated, any one of the two (2)
following materials:
         a.   ABS (Acrylonitrile-Butadiene-Styrene) pipe as specified in
paragraph 6.
         b.   PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) pipe as specified in paragraph 5.
         c.   SR (Rubber Modified Styrene) pipe which must conform to
Commercial Standard CS-228 and meet the Federal Housing Administration Bulletin
UM-26.
      4.   Truss Sewer Pipe: Truss sewer pipe shall be manufactured by
extruding ABS (Acrylonitrile-Butadiene-Styrene) thermoplastic into a truss with
inner and outer walls connected by webs. Joints shall be either a compression
gasket or a chemical weld sleeve. The pipe and joints shall conform to the
requirements of ASTM Specification D-2680.
      5.   Plastic Sewer Pipe And Fittings (For Pressure Or Nonpressure
Systems) Polyvinyl Chloride (PVC) Plastic Pipe (SDR-PR): The Polyvinyl Chloride
(PVC) shall be one hundred twenty five (125) psi or greater, rigid plastic pipe
with integral thickened wall bells. Pipe shall be suitable for use at maximum
hydrostatic working pressure of one hundred twenty five (125) psi at seventy
three degrees Fahrenheit (73°F). All pipe must meet requirements as set forth
in ASTM D-1784. Provisions must be made for contraction and expansion at each
joint with a rubber ring and integral bell as part of each joint and meet the
requirements of ASTM Specification D-1784. PVC pipe with factory installed
couplings or integral thickened wall bells with ring seals will be acceptable.
      6.   Plastic Sewer Pipe And Fittings (For Pressure Or Nonpressure
Systems) Acrylonitrile-Butadiene-Styrene (ABS): The ABS pipe shall be schedule
40 or schedule 80. The pipe shall have integral thickened wall bells. Pipe
shall be suitable for use at maximum hydrostatic working pressure of one
hundred twenty five (125) psi at seventy three degrees Fahrenheit (73°F). All
pipe must meet the requirements as set forth in AST D-1527. Provisions must be
made for contraction and expansion at each joint with a rubber ring and
integral bell as part of each joint. Pipe with factory installed couplings or
integral thickened wall bells with ring seals will be accepted.
   B.   Installation Of Pipelines, Fittings And Accessories: All pipe, fittings
and accessories should be hand-led and lain in strict conformance to the
manufacturer's recommendations.
      1.   General: Pipes shall be laid straight on a minimum slope of one-
eighth inch (1/8") per foot. Each section of the pipe shall rest upon the pipe
bed for the full length of its barrel, with recesses excavated to accommodate
bells and joints. Any pipe that has its grade or joint disturbed after laying
shall be taken up and relaid. The interior of the pipe shall be cleaned of all
foreign matter before being lowered into the trench and shall be kept clean
during laying operations. Under no circumstances shall pipe be laid in water,
and no pipe shall be laid when trench conditions or the weather is unsuitable
for such work, except by permission of the inspector. At all times when work is
not in progress, all open ends of pipe and fittings shall be securely closed to
the satisfaction of the inspector so that no trench water, rodents, earth, or
other substance will enter the pipe or fittings. Any section of pipe already
laid and found to be defective shall be taken up and replaced with new pipe at
the owner's expense. Where sewer lines cross over water lines or if they are
less than eighteen inches (18") lower than water lines, the sewer pipe shall be
ductile iron, for a distance of ten feet (10') each side of the water pipe, or
the sewer pipe shall be encased in concrete at least six inches (6") thick
around the pipe for ten feet (10') each side of the water pipe.
      2.   Cutting And Handling Pipe: Cutting of pipe for closure pieces, or
for other reasons, shall be done by methods which will not damage the pipe. The
pipe shall be handled in such a manner as to ensure delivery in good, undamaged
condition. Particular care shall be exercised not to injure the pipe surfaces
or coatings. Damaged pipe shall not be used in the work.
      3.   Laying The Line: The laying of the sewer line shall commence at the
lowest point along the line with the spigot ends pointing in the direction of
flow. Each length of pipe shall be laid true to line and grade and in such a
manner as to form a close concentric joint with the adjoining pipe to prevent
sudden offsets of the flow line. As the work progresses, the sewer pipe shall
be cleaned of all dirt and other superfluous materials. Where cleaning after
laying is difficult because of small pipe size, suitable swabs or drags shall
be kept in the pipe and pulled forward after each joint is completed. The
proper bends shall be used in order to follow the line and grade desired.
      4.   Pipe Joints: Joints shall be made, using the joining materials and
applied with the proper accessories, in accordance with the manufacturer's
instructions. The joints shall be adjusted and the work performed in a manner
so as to obtain the degree of water rightness required, as specified. As the
joints are progressively made, sufficient backfill should be placed along the
barrel of each pipe to hold it in place while the next joint or joints are
made. All branch lines shall be connected using a forty five degree (45°) Y.
The Y-branch shall enter in the direction of flow. Plugs for future connections
shall be of a permanent type and approved by the inspector. Drains, control
valves, and controlling devices shall be installed in the pipelines where
called for on the drawings, indicated on the ground, or designated by the
inspector.
      5.   Testing: Testing shall be done in the presence of the inspector on
all pipelines installed according to one of the respective tests below. Testing
may be waived by the inspector.
         a.   Pressure Lines: These lines shall be flushed clean and filled
with water, being careful to eliminate all entrapped air, and brought up to an
internal pressure of 1.5 total design head at the low point in the line. The
allowable leakage per one hundred (100) joints per hour for three inch (3")
pipe will be 0.37 gallons; for four inch (4") pipe, 0.50 gallons; for six inch
(6") pipe, 0.75 gallons. This pressure and leakage test shall be run for a
minimum of eight (8) hours. If the test leakage in any section is greater than
that permitted, the leaks shall be located, repairs made, and the section of
pipeline retested until the leakage is within the permitted allowance. Any
visible leak shall be repaired.
         b.   Leakage Tests On Gravity Lines:
            (1)   Each section of the line shall be flushed and cleaned before
it shall be hydrostatically tested upon completion by plugging the lower end of
the section to be tested and the inlet pipe(s) with stopper and filling the
pipe with water.
            (2)   Sewer lines will not be acceptable where the loss of water
exceeds 0.02 gallons per minute, per inch diameter, per one thousand feet
(1,000') of line being tested. All observable leaks shall be repaired even
though the total leakage exceeds the allowable, the pipe shall be overhauled,
and, if necessary, relaid until the test proves satisfactory. If the difference
in head between manholes is excessive, contractor may have to test using pipe
stoppers or he may elect to use only an air test.
            (3)   If the pipe installation fails to meet these requirements,
the pipe shall be overhauled and, if necessary, relaid until the test proves
satisfactory.
      6.   Damage To System: Any existing improvements which may be interfered
with or injured in any way in making such taps, connections, or installations
shall be restored in as good a condition as they were in before such
interference or injury.
      7.   Surface Drainage: No connection shall be constructed in such a
manner as to permit the entrance of surface drainage, and suitable provision
shall be made to prevent the entrance of mud or silt into any such connection.
(1982 Code § 12.03.010)
8-2C-2: BACKFILLING OF TRENCHES:
Backfilling of sewer system line trenches shall be hard packed with care and
well rammed to prevent the slightest settling of the trenches.
(1982 Code § 12.03.020)
8-2C-3: MAINTENANCE OF INSIDE OF SERVICE LINES:
The inside of every sewer system line connecting with the sewer utility shall
be left smooth and perfectly clean throughout its entire length and the ends of
all lines not to be immediately used shall be securely guarded against the
introduction of earth, sand or other foreign material by bricks and cement or
other watertight and impervious material.
(1982 Code § 12.03.030)
8-2C-4: PROPERTY OWNER RESPONSIBLE FOR COST OF INSTALLING, REPAIRING SERVICE
LINES:
The cost of installing the sewer system line shall be paid by the property
owner. The owners of the property served by a sewer system line shall be
responsible for repairing or replacing such sewer service line when, in the
opinion of the administrative official, such line has become inoperative due to
stoppages, crushing, settlement or any other defect.
(1982 Code § 12.03.040)
8-2C-5: METHOD AND SPECIFICATIONS FOR MAKING CONNECTIONS TO SEWER MAINS:
Whenever a sewer connection shall be made, the required trench shall be opened
an ample width to permit easy inspection and the removal of all rubbish. If
there is no junction piece in the sewer, a connection may be made by inserting
into the sewer a “T” saddle of the size specified in the permit required
therefor. After making the opening, which shall be done with great care so as
to not injure the sewer, all rubbish shall be carefully removed from inside the
main sewer. All connections of one line of sewer pipe with another shall be
made with “Y” branches or “T” saddles and long radius eighth bends. The
interior of each length of pipe and the inside of the last joint shall be made
perfectly clean before the next joint is laid. All joints of vitrified clay
pipe shall be set in an approved mastic type joint filler. Slip on type joints
of a type approved by the Town shall be acceptable. The “T” saddle may be
inserted into the sewer and set even with the inside of the sewer on a bed of
mortar and the opening around the pipe carefully repaired and well plastered
with pipe. A “Y” junction or “T” saddle shall be used and the main sewer left
in as good a condition as before the work was done. When a connection is made
to a sewer main, the service line shall be connected thereto until the
connection has been inspected and approved by the Municipality.
(1982 Code § 12.03.050)
8-2C-6: CONSTRUCTION OF SEWERS IN SUBDIVISIONS:
   A.   Main Extension Contract Required: No sewer shall be constructed in a
platted subdivision until the subdivider and the Municipality have executed a
sewer main extension contract.
(1982 Code § 12.03.060)
   B.   Subdivider To Install Mains After Approval Of Plans And Inspection,
Exception: The subdivider shall install the mains in his subdivision by
contract upon approval of the plans and specifications by the Municipality,
execution of sewer extension contract and Municipal inspection of actual
construction; provided, that the Municipality may elect to install the mains,
in which case the subdivider shall deposit with the Municipality the estimated
cost of the sewer construction, plus engineering and administrative costs. The
Municipality shall then proceed to construct the sewer under contract. If at
any time the actual cost exceeds the amount deposited, the subdivider shall
immediately deposit sufficient funds to complete the work.
(1982 Code § 12.03.070)
   C.   Subdivider To Pay Cost Of Construction Of Mains; Mains To Be Extended
To Farthest Points Of Upgrade: The subdivider shall pay the costs of
construction of all sewer mains and appurtenances to, in and through his
subdivision, except as otherwise provided in this chapter. Sewer mains shall
always be extended to the farthest points upgrade in a platted subdivision so
that the system may be perpetuated.
(1982 Code § 12.03.080)
   D.   Undeveloped Areas: When a subdivider finds it necessary to construct a
sewer through undeveloped areas to serve his platted subdivision, the entire
cost of such sewer line shall be paid by the subdivider unless the oversize
main provisions of subsection B of this section are applicable. At the time of
annexation or as the property abutting such sewer is developed and connections
are made to the sewer, the Municipality may collect a charge per front foot
based upon the original construction cost and if so collected shall reimburse
the original subdivider to the extent of the collections so made; provided,
that in no event shall such reimbursement exceed the total cost of the sewer. A
subdivider's right to reimbursement under the provisions of this section shall
terminate fifteen (15) years after execution of the sewer extension contract.
(1982 Code § 12.03.090)
8-2C-7: EXTENSION OF SEWER TO SERVE PROPERTY WITHIN MUNICIPALITY NOT PART OF
SUBDIVISION:
Extension of sewers to serve property within the Municipality, but not a part
of a subdivision, shall be financed by special assessments against the
benefitted property or under such terms and conditions as the governing body
shall provide.
(1982 Code § 12.03.100)
8-2C-8: NONGRAVITY LINES:
   A.   Pumping Stations Generally: When pumping stations are required, the
cost of constructing such stations shall be the responsibility of the property
served thereby. In those instances where it appears that more than one
subdivision may be served by the pump station, the Municipality may require a
larger capacity than that necessary to serve the initial development. Where
such larger capacity is required the additional cost may be paid by the sewer
utility and thereafter collected from other property owners or subdividers
connecting to lines served by the pump station. Such charges shall be paid
prior to the time any connections are made.
(1982 Code § 12.03.110)
   B.   Force Mains Serving Areas Not Otherwise Able To Enter Sewer Utility:
Force mains required to serve an area not otherwise able to enter the
Municipality's sewerage system shall be constructed at the expense of the
owners of the property to be served thereby. (1982 Code § 12.03.120)
   C.   Tie Into Gravity Lines: In those instances where pumping stations and
force mains are required, the sewerage system shall be designed so as to permit
an eventual connection into a gravity system with a minimum of expense. Where
practicable, easements shall be provided and lines constructed to tie into the
gravity system. The Municipality may require deposits, where deemed necessary,
from the property owners requiring such force system to ensure the eventual
construction of gravity lines.
(1982 Code § 12.03.130)
8-2C-9: EXTENSION OF SERVICE OUTSIDE MUNICIPALITY:
   A.   Authority Of Governing Body: The governing body may, in its sole
discretion, enter into agreements with customers whose lands lie outside the
corporate limits, to extend the Municipality's sewer system for the use, needs
and requirements of such customers.
(1982 Code § 12.03.140)
   B.   Findings Prerequisite To Agreement:
      1.   The extension of sewer service is economically feasible.
      2.   The property to be served is readily adaptable to and can be made to
conform, within a reasonable time to be fixed by the governing body, to the
then existing ordinances of the Municipality which relate to subdivision,
platting, zoning and construction of improvements.
      3.   The property to be served is not currently contiguous to the
Municipality limits and cannot therefore be annexed to the Municipality
pursuant to the laws of the State, but that such property can reasonably be
expected to be annexable to the Municipality within the foreseeable future.
      4.   Such extension would help promote the orderly growth and development
of the Municipality.
      5.   Such extension would help promote the health, safety and welfare of
the citizens of the Municipality.
      6.   Such extension would help promote ecological and aesthetic
considerations in the growth and development of the Municipality.
      7.   Such extension is generally in the best interests of the citizens of
the Municipality.
(1982 Code § 12.03.150)
ARTICLE D. USER FEES AND CHARGES
Section
8-2D-1: Methodology For Determination Of User Charge Classification
8-2D-2: User Charges
8-2D-3: Service Outside Municipality
8-2D-4: Bills, Delivery, Delinquency
8-2D-5: Liability For Sewer Fees
8-2D-6: Lien Against Property
8-2D-7: Fees And Charges
8-2D-1: METHODOLOGY FOR DETERMINATION OF USER CHARGE CLASSIFICATION:
   A.   Determine Total Annual Costs: The Town shall determine the total annual
costs of operation and maintenance of the wastewater system which are necessary
to maintain the capacity and performance during the service life of the
treatment works.
   B.   Included Costs: The total annual cost for operation and maintenance
shall include, but not be limited to, labor, equipment replacement, repairs,
maintenance, necessary modifications, power, sampling, laboratory charges,
capital replacement, and a reasonable contingency fund.
   C.   Scope: Actual computation of user equivalent connection ratings and
determination of monthly user charges shall be in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter.
(1982 Code § 12.04.010)
8-2D-2: USER CHARGES:
   A.   Basic Charge; Equivalent Connection Schedule: The basic charge for
discharge of sewer to the Town sewer system shall be thirty dollars twenty five
cents ($30.25) per month, which shall be adjusted to the number of equivalent
connections utilized by each user on the system minimum being one according to
the schedule and user charge system formula as follows:
(Ord. 322, 6-15-2017)
EQUIVALENT CONNECTION SCHEDULE

station)
