(1982 Code § 9.10.030)
10-7-4: PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT:
   A.   Scope: A planned unit development (PUD) is intended to replace the
rigid requirements of conventional zoning with general appearance and
livability guidelines allowing flexibility and innovation in site planning,
building arrangement and land use relationships, while simultaneously insuring
substantial compliance with the intent and purpose of this title.
   B.   Commission Approval: Planned unit development must be approved by the
Planning and Zoning Commission.
   C.   Preliminary Site Plan: The applicant shall submit a preliminary site
plan, including, but not limited to, the following:
      1.   An explanation of all intended uses.
      2.   Preliminary plat.
      3.   An inventory resource statement, with total area proposed in PUD,
data concerning population to be served, the expected value per unit, sewer and
water capabilities, soil types and composition, geologic analysis, and proposed
pedestrian and automobile circulation patterns.
   D.   Final Plan: After receiving Planning and Zoning Commission approval of
the preliminary plan, the developer shall, within one year, submit a final
plan, including, but not limited to, the final draft of all that is listed in
the preliminary plan.
   E.   Minimum Area: No planned unit development shall have an area of less
than ten (10) acres or forty thousand four hundred seventy (40,470) square
meters.
   F.   Ownership: The development shall be in single or corporate ownership at
the time of the application or the subject of an application filed jointly by
all owners of the property.
   G.   Consent For Withdrawal: No piece of land shall be withdrawn from the
PUD without the consent of all the property owners and the Planning and Zoning
Commission.
   H.   CCRs Submitted: The developer shall prepare and submit to the Planning
and Zoning Commission copies of any special agreements, restrictions,
conditions or covenants which will govern the use, continued protection and
maintenance of the planned unit and any of its common park areas and
facilities.
   I.   Density: The residential density of a PUD district shall not be greater
than six (6) units per acre and coverage not greater than sixty percent (60%).
   J.   Acceptable Plan: Building uses, building locations, lot area, width,
yard, height and coverage regulations proposed, shall be considered and
determined acceptable through the process of approving the site development
plan.
   K.   Survey And Staking Work Permitted: Upon approval of the preliminary
plan, and in accordance therewith, the developer may survey and stake the lots,
roads, and other proposed areas on the PUD site, but may not commence any
further development activity until final approval. The completion of survey and
staking work shall in no way obligate any Town officials to grant final
approval.
   L.   Site Plan Requirements: The general site plan required shall include,
but not be limited to, the following: layout of roads, lots, parks and open
space locations, orientation, spacing, signage and lighting, water supply and
sewage treatment system, natural preservation and drainage areas, landscaping,
fencing and screening, and any information including residential density,
coverage and open space characteristics.
   M.   Open Space: The Planning and Zoning Commission may determine whether
all or a part of stream areas, bodies of water and slopes may or may not be
included as usable open space.
   N.   Ownership, Responsibility Of Open Space: The developer may retain
ownership and responsibility for maintenance of the designated open space, and
shall commit himself through written agreement with all parties who
subsequently acquire ownership of property within the PUD.
   O.   Phase Development: All planned unit development may be developed in
phases. No construction of any kind shall begin in the second or subsequent
phases until sixty five percent (65%) of the total development has been sold on
the preceding phase. Development of any phase must be substantially completed
within two (2) years from the time of its final approval.
(1982 Code § 9.10.040)
10-7-5: YARD SPACE FOR ONE BUILDING:
For the purpose of complying with the provisions of this title, no required
yard or other open space for any building, nor any yard or other required open
space on an adjoining lot, shall be considered as providing a yard or open
space on a lot whereon a building is to be erected or established.
(1982 Code § 9.10.050)
10-7-6: UNOBSTRUCTED YARDS:
Every part of a required yard shall be open to the sky except for accessory
buildings in a rear yard, the ordinary projections of skylights, sills, belt
courses, cornices, roof overhang, chimneys, flues and other ornamental features
which project into a yard not more than four feet (4') or 1.22 meters. Also
excepted are open or lattice enclosed fire escapes, fireproof outside stairways
and balconies upon fire towers projecting into a yard, not more than five feet
(5') or 1.52 meters.
(1982 Code § 9.10.070)
10-7-7: WALL OR FENCE:
No fence or wall or other similar structure shall be erected in any required
front, rear or side yard to a height in excess of six feet (6') or 1.83 meters.
(1982 Code § 9.10.080)
10-7-8: MINIMUM BUILDING HEIGHT:
No building shall be erected to a height less than one story above grade.
(1982 Code § 9.10.090)
10-7-9: VIEW OF INTERSECTING STREETS:
In all districts which require a front yard, no obstruction of view in excess
of two feet (2') or .66 meters in height shall be placed on any corner lot
within a triangular area formed by the street property lines and the line
connecting them at points forty feet (40') or 12.19 meters from the
intersection of the street lines, except trees pruned high enough to permit
unobstructed vision by automobile drivers.
(1982 Code § 9.10.100)
10-7-10: COVERAGE:
In no zone except Commercial District (C-1) shall a building or group of
buildings with their accessory buildings cover more than sixty percent (60%) of
the area of the lot. Accessory buildings in a residential district shall not
cover more than twenty five percent (25%) of the rear yard.
(1982 Code § 9.10.110)
10-7-11: KEEPING OF ANIMALS:
   A.   Horses, Cattle: Horses and cattle may be maintained in any zoning
district; provided, that such animals are kept or maintained for noncommercial
use; and further provided, that such animals are confined within fences or
other enclosures at all times, in a manner that does not cause nuisance to
adjacent or neighboring property owners.
   B.   Other Livestock: Other livestock, including, but not limited to,
chickens, goats, pigs, sheep and rabbits shall be allowed in any zoning
district; provided, that such animals are kept or maintained for noncommercial
use; and further provided, that such animals are permanently confined within an
enclosed agricultural structure at all times.
   C.   Sanitation: In the care or maintenance of any authorized or permitted
animals, any person responsible for the care, custody or control of such
animals shall at all times keep and maintain the premises, barn, pen, place or
enclosure where such animals are kept in a clean and sanitary condition, and
shall remove all manure and waste periodically or when requested to do so by
the Town or any local or State health authority, and shall dispose of the same
by spreading it on farm or garden land or otherwise as might be ordered by the
Town or health authority, to render the same sanitary and unoffensive.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1984)
10-7-12: TRAVEL TRAILERS:
   A.   There shall be no limit on the number of occupied travel trailers or
recreational vehicles on any property in any fourteen (14) day period if none
of such trailers or vehicles is maintained on such property for more than seven
(7) consecutive days; provided, that all such vehicles and the occupants
thereof shall not create a nuisance for neighboring residents;
   B.   Only one occupied travel trailer or recreational vehicle shall be
allowed on any lot or parcel of land for more than seven (7) consecutive days
in any fourteen (14) day period without the approval of the Planning and Zoning
Commission;
   C.   No travel trailer or recreational vehicle which is occupied shall be
kept or maintained on any lot or parcel or land for more than thirty (30) days
without the approval of the Planning and Zoning Commission;
   D.   Except in approved sites, no compensation, either direct or indirect,
shall be paid for the location and maintenance of any travel trailer or
recreational vehicle on any property with the Town, nor shall any travel
trailer or recreational vehicle be placed, kept or maintained on any property
within the Town and occupied by any person as employment compensation.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1984)
10-7-13: IMPROVEMENTS REQUIRED:
All lots shall have Town approved water supply and sewage treatment system.
(1982 Code § 9.10.130)
10-7-14: LOT MAINTENANCE:
   A.   Grounds, buildings and structures shall be maintained free of insect
and rodent harborage and infestation. The lot shall be maintained free of
accumulations of debris which may provide rodent harborage or breeding places
for flies, mosquitoes and other pests. Storage areas shall be so maintained as
to prevent rodent harborage.
   B.   Where the potential for insect an rodent infestation exists, all
exterior openings in or beneath any structure shall be appropriately screened
with wire mesh or other suitable materials. All grass and weeds shall be cut
and maintained to prevent fire hazards. The Mayor or the Mayor’s authorized
representative is authorized and empowered to notify in writing the owner or
owners of any lot, place or area within the Town to remove or exterminate weeds
or grass causing fire hazard. Such notice shall be by certified mail, addressed
to the owner at the address used to mail County tax notices, and shall give the
owner such period of time as stated in the notice, not less than ten (10) days
from the receipt of the notice, to remove or exterminate the grass or weeds
causing a fire hazard.
   C.   Upon the failure or refusal of any owner so notified to exterminate or
remove the grass or weeds causing a fire hazard, or more than ten (10) days
after the date of such notice in the event the same is returned to the Town
because of inability to make delivery thereof, the authorized representative of
the Town is authorized to exterminate or remove such weeds or grass causing a
fire hazard and to report to the Town Clerk the same, together with a voucher
of the cost of such extermination and removal, plus twenty percent (20%) to
cover the cost of administration and notice. The Town Clerk shall charge the
cost of such extermination and removal to the property owner or owners and such
special assessment shall become a lien upon and against the lots or parcels of
land and collectible as such.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1984)
10-7-15: MEASURING SETBACKS:
The building setbacks will be measured from the point of the building that
protrudes the closest to the property line on all sides. This does not include
flat sidewalks.
(Ord. 198, 9-9-1996)
10-7-16: SHIPPING CONTAINERS:
   A.   Definition: A cargo storage/shipping container shall be defined as any
large box structure formerly used, or designed to be used, to store and/or haul
cargo by rail, semi-truck, or ship.
   B.   No cargo storage/shipping containers shall be kept, stored, or
maintained within the city limits of the Town of Thayne except in the following
designated areas and as regulated in this section:
      1.   Commercial District C-1.
      2.   Commercial District C-2.
      3.   Industrial District I-1.
(Ord. 391, - -2024)
CHAPTER 8: NONCONFORMING USES AND BUILDINGS
Section
10-8-1: Nonconforming Uses And Buildings
10-8-2: Permits For Expansion Of Nonconforming Uses
10-8-1: NONCONFORMING USES AND BUILDINGS:
   A.   May Be Continued: Except as provided in this chapter, the lawful use
and location of any building or land existing prior to the effective date
hereof may be continued even though the use or location does not conform to the
requirements of this title.
(1982 Code § 9.04.040)
   B.   Maintenance, Repair Permitted: Normal maintenance, repairs and partial
or fully replacement or reconstruction of a building or other structure
containing a nonconforming use is permitted.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1984)
   C.   Parking: A building or structure lacking sufficient automobile parking
space in connection therewith, as required by this title, may be altered or
enlarged, provided additional automobile parking space is supplied to meet the
requirements of this title for such alteration or enlargement.
   D.   Nonconforming Use Vacancy: A building or structure or portion thereof
occupied by a nonconforming use, which is, or hereafter becomes, vacant and
remains unoccupied for a continuous period of six (6) months, shall not
thereafter be occupied except by a use which conforms to the use regulations of
the district in which is it located.
   E.   Occupancy Time Limit: A vacant building or structure may be occupied by
a use for which the building or structure was designed or intended if so
occupied within a period of six (6) months after the use became nonconforming.
(1982 Code § 9.04.040)
   F.   Change Requires To Conforming Use: The nonconforming use of a building
or structure or land may not be changed except to a conforming use; but where
such change is made, the use shall not thereafter be changed back to a
nonconforming use. In the event that any nonconforming use of land is abandoned
for a period of six (6) months or more, any future use of such land shall be in
accordance with applicable district regulations.
   G.   Expansion, Extension: A nonconforming use of land or a nonconforming
building or structure may be expanded or extended in accordance with the
provisions hereof. An application to expand or extend a nonconforming use shall
be submitted in accordance with the provisions of this chapter pertaining to
expansion of nonconforming uses.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1984)
   H.   Mobile Homes: A nonconforming mobile home owner may remove and replace
his mobile home, provided replacement occurs within a period of three (3)
months of the date on which the mobile home was removed.
   I.   Temporary Mobile Homes During Construction: A nonconforming mobile home
may be used as a temporary dwelling during the construction of a permanent
residence for a time period not to exceed eighteen (18) months.
(1982 Code § 9.04.040)
10-8-2: PERMITS FOR EXPANSION OF NONCONFORMING USES:
In order to provide the flexibility necessary to achieve the objectives of this
title and to ensure that owners of nonconforming uses and properties are not
deprived of the ability to reasonably expand nonconforming uses in a manner
which does not cause unreasonable nuisance to neighboring landowners and
residents, the limited expansion of such uses shall be permitted subject to the
granting of a permit as set forth in this section.
   A.   Application: Any person desiring to expand a nonconforming use shall
make application therefor to the Planning and Zoning Commission, and the
application shall contain at least the following information:
      1.   The name and address of the owner and/or applicant;
      2.   A description of the property;
      3.   A description of the existing nonconforming use and the proposed
expansion of such use.
   B.   Commission Hearing: Upon receipt of an application for expansion of a
nonconforming use the Planning and Zoning Commission shall set a date for a
hearing on the application. Notice of such hearing shall be given to all
adjacent property owners by the applicant and proof thereof shall be submitted
by the applicant prior to the hearing date.
   C.   Impacts To Consider: Before acting upon an application for the
expansion of a nonconforming use, the Planning and Zoning Commission shall
consider the following impacts of the proposed expansion:
      1.   The impact of the expanded nonconforming use upon neighboring
properties and uses, including traffic, noise, dust, odors and similar impacts;
      2.   The effect of the expanded nonconforming use on public safety,
traffic flow and control, snow removal and street maintenance;
      3.   Such other impacts as the Planning and Zoning Commission deems
applicable to the proposed expansion.
   D.   Required Findings: Before granting a permit for the expansion of a
nonconforming use, the Commission shall make the following findings:
      1.   That the proposed expansion will not cause unacceptable impacts upon
neighboring property owners and residents;
      2.   That the proposed expansion and the conditions under which the
nonconforming use will be operated will not be detrimental to the public
health, safety or welfare, or materially injurious to property or improvements
in the vicinity.
   E.   Action By Commission: Within thirty (30) days after the hearing on the
application, the commission shall act upon the application. The Commission may
approve the application as submitted, approve the application subject to such
modifications or conditions as the Commission deems necessary to accomplish the
purposes of this section, or the Commission may deny the application.
Conditions imposed by the Commission for approval may include, but shall not be
limited to, special setbacks, screening and limitations upon hours of
operation.
   F.   Submittal To Council; Decision Of Council: Within seven (7) days after
the Commission’s decision, the Commission shall transmit its decision to the
applicant and the Town Council. At its next regularly scheduled meeting
following receipt of the decision, the Town Council shall review the action of
the Commission, and shall affirm, modify or reverse the decision of the
Commission. If the Town Council determines that additional information is
necessary in order to act upon the decision of the Commission, the Town Council
may require further information and may, at its option, hold an additional
hearing upon the application. The Town Council shall consider the same impacts
and make the same findings required for action by the Commission under this
section.
(Ord. 129, 2-27-1994)
CHAPTER 9: TRAVEL TRAILERS AND TRAVEL TRAILERS PARKS
Section
   
10-9-1: Purpose
   
10-9-2: Location And Use
   
10-9-3: Approval Requirements
   
10-9-4: Development Plan
10-9-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to permit development of facilities for travel
trailers in appropriate commercial districts and to require that travel trailer
accommodations be of such character as to promote the objectives and purposes
of this title, to protect the integrity and characteristics of the districts
contiguous to those in which travel trailer parks are located, and to protect
other use values contiguous to or near travel trailer park uses.
(Ord. 381, - -2023)
10-9-2: LOCATION AND USE:
   A.   Approved and Licensed Travel Trailer Park: No travel trailer shall be
located, placed, used or occupied for residential purposes in any district,
except within approved and licensed travel trailer/mobile home parks, except as
otherwise provided herein.
   B.   General Permitted Locations: Travel trailer parks generally shall be
located:
      1.   Adjacent to or in close proximity to a major traffic artery or
highway.
      2.   In a Commercial District.
      3.   No AR-1 or AR-2 adjacent location.
   C.   Maximum Term: No individual space in a travel trailer park shall be
used by one individual trailer for more than one hundred eighty (180)
consecutive days, nor shall such space be rented or leased to any one
individual for a period longer than one hundred eighty (180) days.
   D.   Prohibited As Permanent Residence: Travel trailers may be stored, but
not used for permanent living quarters.
   E.   Sales Lots: Travel trailers may be stored, displayed, sold and
serviced, but not used for living quarters, in a sales lot in a commercial or
manufacturing district, when such use is a permitted or a conditional use.
   F.   Location Within Mobile Home Park: Travel trailers may be accommodated
in an approved and licensed mobile home park;
   G.   Temporary Residence: Travel trailers may be used as a temporary
residence in the AR-1 and AR-2 zoning districts by the property owner. A
temporary use permit may be granted while construction of permanent residence
is being. A temporary use permit may be issued by the Town council, with a
written plan to address the following:
      1.   Approved septic connection to Town’s sewer system.
      2.   Adequate fire protection as required by the Mid Valley Fire
District.
      3.   Approved water connection to Town’s water system.
      4.   Adequate power source as approved by the local utility company.
(Ord. 381, - -2023)
10-9-3: APPROVAL REQUIREMENTS:
A travel trailer park may not be constructed unless first approved by the
planning commission after review of plans for said travel trailer park which
satisfy the planning commission that the proposed development will:
   A.   District Character: Be in keeping with the general character of the
commercial district with which the proposed development will be located.
   B.   Minimum Area: Be located on a parcel of land containing not less than
one-half (1/2) acre.
   C.   Occupancy: Have at least two (2) spaces completed and ready for
occupancy before the first occupancy is permitted.
   D.   Compliance With Requirements: Meet all requirements of this title and
specifically this chapter.
   E.   State Requirements: Meet all state requirements relating to camp,
trailer, hotel, motel and resort sanitation regulations which are intended to
apply to trailer, camper and tent camps, as defined in such code.
   F.   Density: Contain no more than six (6) units per acre. The spaces may be
clustered; provided, that the total number of spaces does not exceed the number
permitted on one-half acre, multiplied by the number of acres in the
development. The remaining land not contained in individual spaces, roads or
parking, shall be set aside and developed as parks, playgrounds and/or service
areas for the common use and enjoyment of occupants of the development and
visitors thereto.
(Ord. 381, - -2023)
10-9-4: DEVELOPMENT PLAN:
An overall plan for development of a travel trailer park shall be submitted to
the planning commission for review. The plan shall be drawn to scale. The plan
shall show:
   A.   The topography of the site, when required by the planning commission,
represented by contours shown at not greater than two foot (2') intervals.
   B.   The proposed street and trailer/home space pad layout, including points
of ingress and egress.
   C.   Proposed reservations for parks, playgrounds and open spaces.
   D.   Tabulations showing the percent of area to be devoted to parks,
playgrounds and open spaces, the number of trailer spaces, and the total area
to be developed.
   E.   Proposed location, number and design of parking spaces.
   F.   Generalized landscaping and utility plan, including location of water,
electricity, gas lines and fire hydrants.
   G.   Any other data the planning and zoning commission may require.
(Ord. 381, - -2023)
CHAPTER 10: MOBILE HOMES PARKS
Section
   
10-10-1: Purpose
   
10-10-2: Location And Use
   
10-10-3: Approval Requirements
   10-10-4: Development Plan
10-10-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to permit development of facilities for mobile
homes in appropriate commercial districts and to require that mobile home
accommodations be of such character as to promote the objectives and purposes
of this title, to protect the integrity and characteristics of the districts
contiguous to those in which mobile home parks are located, and to protect
other use values contiguous to or near mobile home park uses.
(Ord. 382, - -2023)
10-10-2: LOCATION AND USE:
   A.   Approved and Licensed Mobile Home Park: No mobile home shall be
located, placed, used or occupied for residential purposes in any district,
except within approved and licensed mobile home/mobile home parks, except as
otherwise provided herein.
   B.   General Permitted Locations: Mobile home parks generally shall be
located:
      1.   Adjacent to or in close proximity to a major traffic artery or
highway.
      2.   In a Commercial District.
      3.   No AR-1 or AR-2 adjacent location.
(Ord. 382, - -2023)
10-10-3: APPROVAL REQUIREMENTS:
A mobile home park may not be constructed unless first approved by the planning
commission after review of plans for said mobile home park which satisfy the
planning commission that the proposed development will:
   A.   District Character: Be in keeping with the general character of the
commercial district with which the proposed development will be located.
   B.   Minimum Area: Be located on a parcel of land containing not less than
one (1) acre.
   C.   Occupancy: Have at least four (4) spaces completed and ready for
occupancy before the first occupancy is permitted.
   D.   Compliance With Requirements: Meet all requirements of this title and
specifically this chapter.
   E.   Density: Contain no more than five (5) units per acre. The spaces may
be clustered; provided, that the total number of spaces does not exceed the
number permitted on one acre, multiplied by the number of acres in the
development. The remaining land not contained in individual spaces, roads or
parking, shall be set aside and developed as parks, playgrounds and/or service
areas for the common use and enjoyment of occupants of the development and
visitors thereto.
(Ord. 382, - -2023)
10-10-4: DEVELOPMENT PLAN:
An overall plan for development of a mobile home park shall be submitted to the
planning commission for review. The plan shall be drawn to scale. The plan
shall show:
   A.   The topography of the site, when required by the planning commission,
represented by contours shown at not greater than two foot (2') intervals.
   B.   The proposed street and trailer/home space pad layout, including points
of ingress and egress.
   C.   Proposed reservations for parks, playgrounds and open spaces.
   D.   Tabulations showing the percent of area to be devoted to parks,
playgrounds and open spaces, the number of trailer spaces, and the total area
to be developed.
   E.   Proposed location, number and design of parking spaces.
   F.   Generalized landscaping and utility plan, including location of water,
electricity, gas lines and fire hydrants.
   G.   Any other data the planning and zoning commission may require.
(Ord. 382, - -2023)
TITLE 11: SUBDIVISION OF LAND
GENERAL PROVISIONS   1
EXEMPTIONS   2
ENGINEERING REVIEWS   3
SIMPLE SUBDIVISIONS   4
GENERAL SUBDIVISIONS   5
IMPROVEMENT COMPLETION ASSURANCE   6
WARRANTY   7
DESIGN STANDARDS   8
RECAPTURE FEE ORDINANCE   9
Statutory reference:
   Statute authority, see WS § 15-1-501 et seq.
CHAPTER 1: GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section
11-1-1: Title And Authority
11-1-2: Purpose
11-1-3: Definitions
11-1-1: TITLE AND AUTHORITY:
No Person shall subdivide any tract of land in the Town of Thayne (Town),
except in conformity with the provisions of this Title.
Adoption of this Title supersedes any and all previous Town subdivision
ordinances. An applicant may process applications related to subdivisions as
outlined in this Title. Nothing in this ordinance shall exempt applicants from
the minimum requirements outlined in the Wyoming State Statutes.
Effective 8/17/2022 any subdividing of property will be based upon the recorded
plats with Lincoln County on this date.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-1-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to:
   A.   Provide for the health, safety, and welfare of the residents of the
Town.
   B.   Promote the prosperity of the Town.
   C.   Improve the morals, peace, good order, comfort, convenience, and
aesthetics of the town for all inhabitants and businesses.
   D.   Ensure a sound tax base and protect property values.
   E.   Protect both urban and nonurban development.
   F.   Provide fundamental fairness in land use regulation.
   G.   Facilitate orderly growth.
   H.   Ensure the development of economically sound and compatible
neighborhoods.
   I.   Ensure the construction of necessary improvements and utilities.
   J.   Ensure safe and convenient circulation of vehicular and pedestrian
traffic.
   K.   Ensure development is in accordance with the requirements of the Town’s
General Plan.
   L.   Ensure that new development bears its fair share of the costs of
providing improvements and services necessitated by, or resulting from, the
development of subdivisions.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-1-3: DEFINITIONS:
APPLICANT: A property owner, or the property owner’s designee, who submits a
land use application regarding the property owner’s land.
DEVELOPMENT ACTIVITY:
   1.   Any construction or expansion of a building, structure, or use that
creates additional demand and need for public facilities;
   2.   Any change in use of a building or structure that creates additional
demand and need for public facilities; or
   3.   Any change in the use of land that creates additional demand and need
for public facilities.
EASEMENT: That portion of a lot or lots reserved or granted for the present or
future use by a person or agency other than the legal owner or owners of said
properties. The easement may be for use under, on, or above said lots.
FINAL PLAT: The final drawing of the subdivision and dedication prepared for
filing for record with the Clerk of Lincoln County and in compliance with all
the requirements set forth in state code and this title.
GENERAL PLAN: A document that Town adopted that sets forth general guidelines
for proposed future development of the land within the Town.
IMPROVEMENT COMPLETION ASSURANCE OR ASSURANCES: A surety bond, letter of credit
or cash required to guaranty the proper completion of infrastructure
improvement.
IMPROVEMENT WARRANTY: An applicant’s unconditional warranty that the
applicant’s installed and accepted infrastructure improvement:
   1.   Complies with the Town’s written standards for design, materials, and
workmanship; and
   2.   Will not fail in any material respect, as a result of poor workmanship
or materials, within the improvement warranty period.
IMPROVEMENT WARRANTY PERIOD: A period no later than one year after the Town’s
acceptance of required infrastructure.
INFRASTRUCTURE IMPROVEMENT: Permanent infrastructure that is essential for the
public health and safety or that:
   1.   Is required for human occupation; and
   2.   An applicant must install:
      a.   In accordance with published installation and inspection
specifications for public improvements; and
      b.   Whether the improvement is public or private, as a condition of:
         (1)   Recording a subdivision plat;
         (2)   Obtaining a building permit; or
         (3)   Development of a commercial, industrial, mixed use, condominium,
or multifamily project.
LOT. A tract of land, regardless of any label, that is created by and shown on
a subdivision plat that has been recorded in the office of the Clerk of Lincoln
County.
LOT LINE ADJUSTMENT. A relocation of a lot line boundary between adjoining lots
or between a lot and adjoining parcels.
MAY: Can be done or allowed, optional.
MUNICIPAL UTILITY EASEMENT. An easement that:
   1.   Is created or depicted on a plat recorded in a county clerk’s office
and is described as a municipal utility easement granted for public use;
   2.   Is not a protected utility easement or a public utility easement as
defined in Wyoming State Code;
   3.   The Town or the Town’s affiliated governmental entity uses and occupies
to provide a utility service, including sanitary sewer, culinary water,
electrical, storm water, or communications or data lines;
   4.   Is used or occupied with the consent of the Town in accordance with an
authorized franchise or other agreement;
   5.   Is used or occupied by a specified public utility in accordance with an
authorized franchise or other agreement; and is located in a utility easement
granted for public use.
PARCEL: Any real property that is not a lot.
PHASING: The orderly and logical division of a preliminary plat map/subdivision
map to provide for recordation of portions of a plat map/subdivision map at
differing time periods.
PLANNING AND ZONING BOARD: The Town’s Planning and Zoning Board. If the Town
does have an active Planning and Zoning Board, the Town Council may act as the
Planning and Zoning Board.
PLAT: An instrument subdividing property into lots as depicted on a map or
other graphical representation of lands that a licensed professional land
surveyor makes and prepares.
PRELIMINARY PLAT: A map or maps of a proposed subdivision and specified
supporting materials, drawn and submitted in accordance with this title and
state code, to permit the evaluation of the proposal prior to detailed
engineering and design.
PUBLIC HEARING: A hearing at which members of the public are provided a
reasonable opportunity to comment on the subject of the hearing.
PUBLIC MEETING: A meeting that is required to be open to the public that the
public can attend.
PUBLIC STREET: A public right-of-way, including a public highway, public
avenue, public boulevard, public parkway, public road, public lane, public
alley, public viaduct, public subway, public tunnel, public bridge, public
byway, other public transportation easement, or other public way.
RECORD OF SURVEY MAP: A map of a survey of land prepared in accordance with
Wyoming State Code.
RIGHT-OF-WAY: A right-of-way that has been established by either deed,
conveyance or court order.
SHALL: Must, mandatory, required to be done.
STATE: Includes any department, division, or agency of the state.
SUBDIVISION: Any land that is divided, re-subdivided, or proposed to be divided
into two or more lots or other division of land for the purpose, whether
immediate or future, for offer, sale, lease, or development either on the
installment plan or upon any and all other plans, terms, and conditions.
ZONING ADMINISTRATOR: The person designated by the Town Council to administer
the subdivision process in the Town. The person could be the mayor, other town
official, or a Town employee.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 2: EXEMPTIONS
Section
11-2-1: Exemptions
11-2-1: EXEMPTIONS:
This title shall not apply to:
   A.   The transfer of any parcel of land by order of court.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 3: ENGINEERING REVIEWS
Section
11-3-1: Licensed Engineer
11-3-2: Engineering Fees
11-3-1: LICENSED ENGINEER:
The Town Engineer will be licensed within the State to review, supervise and
inspect the construction of all public improvements within the Town, in order
to ensure such improvements are constructed in accordance with the Town
standard specifications and this title. The developer will not materially
deviate from the improvement plans, standard specifications or this title
without the express written approval of the Town.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-3-2: ENGINEERING FEES:
The developer shall pay for the fees incurred by the Town to retain the Town
Engineer to review plans and inspect the construction of all public
improvements. The Town shall provide the developer with an invoice for such
services on a regular basis. The developer shall pay for such engineering costs
within thirty (30) days of its receipt of the invoice for the engineering
costs.
(Ord. 248, 6-11-2008; amd. Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 4: SIMPLE SUBDIVISIONS
Section
11-4-1: Applicability
11-4-2: Pre-Application Conference
11-4-3: Simple Subdivision Application
11-4-4: Simple Subdivision Final Plat
11-4-5: Simple Subdivision Application And Final Plat Consideration Process
11-4-6: Recordation Of Final Plat
11-4-1: APPLICABILITY:
Simple subdivision requirements shall apply to subdivisions that:
   A.   Create one or two lots, or
   B.   Consolidate one or more lots; or,
   C.   Change a boundary line between two adjoining lots or parcels; or,
   D.   Change a subdivision plat to correct errors in legal descriptions or
monument locations; and
   E.   Require no change in zoning.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-4-2: PRE-APPLICATION CONFERENCE:
The landowner(s) and/or has representative shall meet with the Zoning
Administrator in a pre-application conference and discuss the following:
   A.   The scope of the proposed project and the applicant’s specific
development objectives.
   B.   The applications anticipated project schedule.
   C.   Approvals required by the Town before any development can occur.
   D.   The documents, plans, drawings, fees and other materials that will be
that will be needed to process a complete subdivision application.
   E.   Potential issues associated with the subdivision.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-4-3: SIMPLE SUBDIVISION APPLICATION:
Applicant shall file simple subdivision application form with the Town Clerk.
The application shall include the following:
   A.   Name and address of the owner and applicant.
   B.   Legal description of the property to be subdivided.
   C.   A copy of the deed and easements pertaining to the property.
   D.   Existing zoning for the property.
   E   A list of all landowners who own property within 300 feet of the
proposed subdivision.
   F.   Site plan including but not limited to existing and proposed streets,
existing structures, irrigation facilities, existing and proposed utilities
(water, sewer, power, communications), topography, existing and proposed storm
drainage structure.
   G.   Planned water system, as well as anticipated average day and maximum
day water demand and fire flow requirements.
   H.   Planned wastewater system, as well as anticipated average daily flows.
   I.   Filing fees.
(Ord. 373, - -2022; amd. Ord. 384, - -2023)
11-4-4: SIMPLE SUBDIVISION FINAL PLAT:
The final plat map shall be prepared and signed by a Wyoming licensed surveyor
and include the following:
   A.   The proposed subdivision name. (It must be distinct from any other plat
recorded in the County. North arrow required.)
   B.   Details of proposed development. All lots shall have clear dimensions,
boundaries and liner footages of lot width and depth. Square footage of each
lot shall be clearly shown in hundredths of an acre (and square foot for lots
less than 0.5 acres in size).
   C.   All survey monument locations and related survey information.
   D.   Any street dedications, street names and street dimensions.
   E.   Any areas dedicated for public use or purpose.
   F.   Length and width of blocks.
   G.   Any existing structures.
   H.   Every existing right-of-way and recorded easements for any underground
facilities, water conveyance facility or any other utility facility.
   I.   Any other utility facility or roadway that is not recorded that the
owner or applicant has knowledge of.
   J.   Any other information that the owner or applicant has constructive
knowledge of including information from the state engineers’ office, from any
surveys done on the subject property, from FEMA or the Army Corps of Engineers.
   K.   The approval signature blocks for the owner, surveyor, Clerk, Mayor,
and Clerk of Lincoln County. All signatures shall be on the final plat and the
owner(s) signature(s) must be notarized.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-4-5: SIMPLE SUBDIVISION APPLICATION AND FINAL PLAT CONSIDERATION PROCESS:
   A.   The Zoning Administrator shall review the final plat for completeness
and conformance with applicable Town codes, development standards, and design
criteria and prepare a staff report with recommendations.
   B.   The Town Clerk shall notify, in writing, all landowners of properties
that are located within 300 feet of the proposed subdivision. This notice will
generally advise landowners of the proposed subdivision, and the date when any
written comments from the general public are to be received. The deadline for
written comments shall be two weeks from the date of the date of the mailing.
   C.   The Town Planning and Zoning Board shall review and discuss the
recommendations of the Zoning Administrator. No public hearing will be
required. Subsequently, the Town Planning and Zoning Board shall approve,
recommend approval of the proposed subdivision; or denial of the proposed
subdivision. In the event that further information is desired by the Town
Planning and Zoning Board, any decision of the Town Planning and Zoning Board
may be tabled until members of the Planning and Zoning Board have had
sufficient opportunity to review and evaluate the information.
   D.   The Town Council shall review the recommendation of the Town Planning
and Zoning Board. The Town Council shall, approve, approve with conditions or
modifications; or deny the proposed subdivision.
   E.   The Zoning Administrator shall issue a written notice of determination
to the applicant within five (5) business days of the decision of the Town
Council. The notice will indicate the decision made and, when appropriate,
conditions that may accompany the approval of a specific application or reasons
why the application was denied.
   F.   Any appeal of the decisions by the Town Planning and Zoning Board shall
be made to the Town Council.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-4-6: RECORDATION OF FINAL PLAT:
The applicant shall have one year from date of Town Council approval to record
the final plat. If the final plat has not been recorded within one year of the
Town Council approval date, the final plat approval shall become null and void.
   A.   All fees shall be paid to the Town prior to recordation of the plat.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
Simple Subdivision Process

CHAPTER 5: GENERAL SUBDIVISIONS
Section
11-5-1: Applicability
11-5-2: Pre-Application Conference
11-5-3: General Subdivision Application
11-5-4: Master Plan Report
11-5-5: Preliminary Plat Application Process
11-5-6: Agency Letters - Requirements
11-5-7: Phasing Of Subdivisions - Preliminary Plat
11-5-8: Preliminary Plat Consideration Process
11-5-9: Approval Time Period And Extension
11-5-10: Developers Agreement
11-5-11: Final Plat Approval
11-5-12: Recordation Of Final Plat
11-5-1: APPLICABILITY:
General subdivision requirements shall apply to subdivisions that:
   A.   Create three or more lots.
   B.   May or may not conform to existing zoning.
   C.   May require the construction of new municipal streets, extension of
municipal water, wastewater, and storm management systems, or the development
of other public improvements.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-2: PRE-APPLICATION CONFERENCE:
The landowner(s) and/or has representative shall meet with the Zoning
Administrator in a pre-application conference and discuss the following:
   A.   The scope of the proposed project and the applicant’s specific
development objectives.
   B.   The applications anticipated project schedule.
   C.   Approvals required by the Town before any development can occur.
   D.   The documents, plans, drawings, fees and other materials that will be
that will be needed to process a complete subdivision application.
   E.   Potential issues associated with the subdivision.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-3: GENERAL SUBDIVISION APPLICATION:
Applicant shall file a general subdivision application and re-zone application
(if applicable) with the Town Clerk. The application shall include the
following:
   A.   Name and address of the owner and applicant.
   B.   Legal description of the property to be subdivided.
   C.   A copy of the deed and easements pertaining to the property.
   D.   Existing zoning for the property.
   E.   A list of all landowners who own property within 300 feet of the
proposed subdivision.
   F.   Filing fees.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-4: MASTER PLAN REPORT:
Applicant shall complete and file a master plan report for the proposed
subdivision with the Town Clerk. The master plan will address what municipal
services the subdivision intends to use, as well as the potential impact of the
proposed subdivision upon the Town and the community. The master plan, which
will contain a combination of technical narrative, statistical tables, and
illustrations, will address, at least, the following issues:
   A.   The purpose of the subdivision and proposed land uses.
   B.   A development schedule for proposed land uses.
   C.   The number of lots being created and, if applicable, the zoning
designations requested for each lot.
   D.   Planned water system, as well as anticipated average day and maximum
day water demand and fire flow requirements.
   E.   Planned wastewater system, as well as anticipated average daily flows.
   F.   Planned points of access to municipal roads, Lincoln County roads, and
U.S. Highway 89, anticipated average and peak day traffic volumes.
   G.   Planned stormwater management plan and anticipated stormwater flows for
10-year storm event.
   H.   Description of soil types, wetland areas, and topography of the site
and discussion of subdivision design considerations related to site conditions.
   I.   Discussion of existing and proposed irrigation systems and water
rights.
   J.   Planned easements to accommodate access to, or the extension of, the
Town’s planned community trail system, if applicable.
   K.   The following detailed engineering reports may be required, as
requested by the Town Engineer. A licensed Wyoming civil engineer shall prepare
the reports:
      1.   Soils Report.
      2.   Storm Drainage Report showing pre and post development runoff
calculations and proposed drainage structures.
      3.   Traffic Study performed in July or August.
(Ord. 373, - -2022; amd. Ord. 384, - -2023)
11-5-5: PRELIMINARY PLAT APPLICATION PROCESS:
Concurrently with the Master Plan Report the applicant shall submit a
preliminary plat. The preliminary plat map shall be prepared and signed by a
Wyoming licensed surveyor and include the following:
   A.   The proposed subdivision name. (It must be distinct from any other plat
recorded in the County. North arrow required.)
   B.   Details of proposed development. (All lots shall have clear dimensions,
boundaries and liner footages of lot width and depth. Square footage of each
lot shall be clearly shown.)
   C.   Any street dedications, street names and lot addresses along with
street dimensions and cross-sections.
   D.   Any areas dedicated for public use or purpose.
   E.   Any private streets with street dimensions and cross-sections.
   F.   Any proposed storm drains.
   G.   Location of any known man-made features on the subject property.
   H.   Location of any existing or known water and sewer infrastructure
(mainlines, valves, manholes, fire hydrants, water and sewer services, etc.)
   I.   Length and width of blocks.
   J.   Any existing structures.
   K.   Every existing right-of-way and recorded easements for any underground
facilities, water conveyance facility or any other utility facility.
   L.   Any other utility facility or roadway that is not recorded that the
owner or applicant has knowledge of.
   M.   Any other information that the owner or applicant has constructive
knowledge of including information from the state engineers’ office, from any
surveys done on the subject property, from FEMA or the Army Corps of Engineers.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-6: AGENCY LETTERS - REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Written acknowledgments of ability to serve the development from the
local fire authority.
   B.   Written comments from Lincoln County.
   C.   Written comments from WYDOT if the subdivision directly accesses
Highway 98, secondary access is within five hundred feet (500') Highway 89, or
if the town deems necessary.
   D.   Written comments from Wyoming State Fire Marshall.
(Ord. 373, - -2022; amd. Ord. 384, - -2023)
11-5-7: PHASING OF SUBDIVISIONS - PRELIMINARY PLAT:
Subdivisions may be phased. Separate phases may be recorded, and infrastructure
constructed per phase subject to the following:
   A.   Phasing shall require the submittal of a phasing plan at the time of
submittal of preliminary plat approval.
   B.   All phases shall be in conformance with the preliminary plat
application and the phasing plan shall provide all necessary information to
fully evaluate the merits of the phasing program.
   C.   Each phase shall stand on its own regarding public improvements, so
that if subsequent phases are not recorded, pre-recorded phases can function
without need of future phased development.
   D.   Temporary public improvements may be required, so that no phase is
dependent upon construction of a subsequent phase.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-8: PRELIMINARY PLAT CONSIDERATION PROCESS:
   A.   Within 45 days of the receipt of a complete application and support
materials, the Zoning Administrator shall provide a written staff report to the
Town Planning and Zoning Board and Town Council that confirms the completeness
of the subdivision application, the receipt of required filing fees, and
potential changes in zoning. Based upon comments received from agencies and
other municipal representatives, this report shall concurrently evaluate the
following:
      1.   Consistency of the proposed subdivision with the Town Municipal
Master Plan;
      2.   Consistency of the proposed subdivision with subdivision development
standards and design criteria outlined in Appendix D of Title 11;
      3.   Compatibility and potential impacts of the proposed subdivision and
related zone change upon adjoining land uses;
      4.   Suitability of the subject and adjacent properties to existing
zoning;
      5.   Potential impacts of the proposed subdivision upon the Town, e.g.,
municipal roads, water system, wastewater system, storm water management, and
other public services; and,
      6.   When applicable, potential land use management issues that may arise
with the establishment of planned covenants, contracts or deed restrictions via
common-interest development.
      7.   The staff report shall also recommend approval of the subdivision as
proposed, approval with some possible modifications to the preliminary plat, or
provide rationale for denial of the preliminary plat and, when applicable, the
related re-zoning request.
   B.   The Town Clerk shall notify, in writing, all landowners of properties
that are located within 300 feet of the proposed major subdivision. This notice
will generally advise landowners of the proposed subdivision, the time and
place of public hearings before the Planning and Zoning Board and Town Council,
and the date when any written comments from the general public are to be
received.
   C.   Upon receiving the staff report from the Zoning Administrator, a public
hearing shall be required at the next regular meeting of the Planning and
Zoning Board, or a special meeting shall be scheduled. The time and place of
the hearing shall be advertised twice, at least, in advance of the hearing in
two or more of the following local newspaper, town website, town social media
account, or public buildings within the town. During the public hearing, the
applicant will provide a brief overview of the proposed subdivision and, when
applicable, the related re-zoning request. Subsequently, the Town Planning and
Zoning Board will receive public comments concerning the proposed subdivision.
   D.   Based upon its evaluation of the master plan, preliminary plat, review
comments from municipal representatives, the staff report, and public comments,
the Town Planning and Zoning Board will discuss the merits, disadvantages, and
potential issues associated with the proposed subdivision and, when applicable,
the related re-zoning request. In the event that further information is desired
by the Planning and Zoning Board, any decision of the Planning and Zoning Board
may be tabled, for not to exceed 30 days, until members of the Planning and
Zoning Board have had sufficient opportunity to review and evaluate any new
information.
   E.   The Town Planning and Zoning Board shall recommend approval, approval
with conditions or modifications, or denial of the proposed subdivision to the
Town Council. The decision to approve or deny the preliminary subdivision plat
and any related re-zoning request shall be concurrent.
   F.   The Town Council shall review and discuss comments from various
municipal representatives, the recommendations of the Zoning Administrator, and
the recommendations of the Planning and Zoning Board. Subsequently, the Town
Council shall approve, approve with conditions or modifications, or deny the
preliminary subdivision plat and, when applicable, the proposed re-zoning
request. In the event that further information is desired by the Town Council,
any decision of the Town Council may be tabled until members of the Town
Council have had sufficient opportunity to review and evaluate any new
information.
   G.   The Zoning Administrator shall issue a written notice of determination
to the applicant within five (5) business days of the decision of the Town
Council. The notice will indicate the decision made and, when appropriate,
conditions that may accompany the approval of the preliminary subdivision plat
and, when applicable, related re-zoning request, or reasons why the plat and
re-zoning requests were denied.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-9: APPROVAL TIME PERIOD AND EXTENSION:
Preliminary plat approval shall remain in effect for a period of one year after
Town Council approval. An extension may be considered by the Planning
Commission and Town Council prior to the expiration of the preliminary plat
approval date.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-10: DEVELOPERS AGREEMENT:
Upon Planning Commission and Town Council approval of the preliminary plat, the
applicant shall prepare and submit a Developers Agreement for review and
approval by the Town Council.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-11: FINAL PLAT APPROVAL:
   A.   Upon approval and execution of the developer’s agreement, the applicant
can submit the final plat application to the Town Council for consideration.
The final plat shall contain all information outlined in Chapter 4B. The final
plat shall also contain the following additional information:
      1.   The proposed subdivision name. (It must be distinct from any other
plat recorded in the County. North arrow required.)
      2.   Details of proposed development. All lots shall have clear
dimensions, boundaries and liner footages of lot width and depth. Square
footage of each lot shall be clearly shown in hundredths of an acre (and square
foot for lots less than 0.5 acres in size).
      3   All survey monument locations and related information.
      4.   Any street dedications, street names and street dimensions.
      5.   Any areas dedicated for public use or purpose.
      6.   Length and width of blocks.
      7.   Any existing structures.
      8.   Every existing right-of-way and recorded easements for any
underground facilities, water conveyance facility or any other utility
facility.
      9.   Any other utility facility or roadway that is not recorded that the
owner or applicant has knowledge of.
      10.   Any other information that the owner or applicant has constructive
knowledge of including information from the state engineers’ office, from any
surveys done on the subject property, from FEMA or the Army Corps of Engineers.
      11.   The approval signature blocks for the owner, surveyor, Clerk,
Mayor, and Clerk of Lincoln County. All signatures shall be on the final plat
and the owner(s) signature(s) must be notarized.
   B.   The Town Council shall not approve the final plat until all the
improvements required by this title have been installed, inspected, or properly
secured as required by Chapter 5.
**If no public infrastructure or other public improvements are required, the
preliminary and final plat may be reviewed concurrently.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
11-5-12: RECORDATION OF FINAL PLAT:
The applicant shall have one year from date of Town Council approval to record
the final plat. If the final plat has not been recorded within one year of the
Town Council approval date, the final plat approval shall become null and void.
   A.   All fees shall be paid to the Town prior to recordation of the plat.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
Appendix C: General Subdivision Process

CHAPTER 6: IMPROVEMENT COMPLETION ASSURANCE
Section
   
11-6-1: Improvement Completion Assurance
11-6-1: IMPROVEMENT COMPLETION ASSURANCE:
   A.   Before an applicant conducts any development, activity or records a
plat, the applicant shall:
      1.   Complete any required infrastructure improvements, or post
improvement completion assurance. If completion assurance is elected the
applicant shall provide completion assurance for:
         a.   Completion of 100 percent of the required infrastructure
improvements or 100 percent of the incomplete or unaccepted infrastructure
improvements.
         b.   This Chapter does not apply if the proposed improvements are
private and not essential to building code, fire code, flood or storm water
management provisions, street and access requirements, or other essential
necessary public safety improvements.
      2.   Completion assurance can be accepted by the Town in the following
forms:
         a.   A bond with a surety company licensed to do business in the State
of Wyoming, having a bond rating of AAA.
         b.   Irrevocable letter of credit from a federally insured
institution.
         c.   Cash deposit.
   B.   Completion assurance shall be in amount that reflects 125 percent of
the anticipated cost of improvements.
   C.   Any of the above forms of assurance must be approved by the Town
Attorney prior to Town acceptance.
      1.   Assurance release
         a.   Assurance may be partially released as portions of required
infrastructure improvements are completed and accepted by the Town.
         b.   Funds held as security shall be released by the Town equal to the
actual cost of performing the work minus ten percent. Partial assurance release
shall be subject to the Town Engineer’s acceptance of a logical completion of
infrastructure improvements required to support the subject development.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 7: WARRANTY
Section
   
11-7-1: Warranty
11-7-1: WARRANTY:
A one-year improvement warranty period is required. Terms of the warranty
period shall be defined in the developers agreement. Once all improvements have
been inspected and accepted by the Town, the one-year improvement warranty
period shall begin. At the time of acceptance, any assurance accepted by the
Town for improvements shall be released (except ten percent). Ten percent of
the assurance amount shall be held by the Town to guarantee the quality of
workmanship and materials during the one-year improvement warranty period.
After one year has elapsed and after the Town inspection reveals no quality or
workmanship issues, the remainder of the assurance shall be released.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 8: DESIGN STANDARDS
Section
   11-8-1: Design Standards
11-8-1: DESIGN STANDARDS:
   A.   Conformity.
      1.   All public improvements shall be in substantial conformity with the
preliminary plat as approved, and in accordance with good engineering and
construction practices. The Town Engineer may modify any design standard if
found necessary to provide for orderly development.
      2.   All public improvements design and construction shall conform to the
Town Public Works Standard Specifications and Drawings
   B.   Streets.
      1.   Streets shall be developed in accordance with the town road
masterplan.
      2.   The subdivider shall be required to make and install improvements to
existing streets within and abutting the subdivision. The improvements do not
include the requirement for street paving of the abutting streets unless it is
determined necessary by the Town Engineer to provide for logical and proper
development.
      3.   Wherever topography will permit, the arrangement of the streets
shall provide for alignment with, and a continuation of, existing streets and
adjoining areas.
      4.   Cul-de-sacs shall terminate in a circular turn-around, have a
minimum right-of-way of at least 120 feet in diameter, and a paved turn-around
with a minimum outside diameter of 100 feet.
         a.   Cul-de-sacs shall be no longer that 700 feet unless otherwise
approved by the Town Engineer.
      5.   Whenever a new street is proposed along the edge of the subdivision,
the entire street shall be dedicated and improved with the subdivision.
      6.   No more than two streets shall intersect at any point.
         a.   A street shall have a minimum straight distance of 100 feet from
the intersection before it may be curved.
      7.   A straight section of 100 feet shall be provided between reverse
curves on all streets.
      8.   All lots in the subdivision will have direct access to a dedicated
street, that has been improved to Town standards and adopted by the Town
subject to the following exception:
         a.   private access drives may be approved for subdivisions with a
total of three or less units in the residential zoning district(s).
      9.   The length of local streets between intersections shall be subject
to a maximum of 1,320 feet.
      10.   The town must approve street names.
      11.   The minimum dedicated right-of-way and roadway section shall be as
follows:
 
Street Classification Minimum Right-of-Way Standard Road Section
Major Collector       70 feet              See Public Works Standards and
                                           Specifications
Minor Collector       60 feet              See Public Works Standards and
                                           Specifications
Local                 60 feet              See Public Works Standards and
                                           Specifications
 
      12.   Subdivisions, which include any part of an existing platted street,
which do not conform to the minimum right-of-way requirements of these
regulations, may be required to provide additional width necessary to meet the
minimum right-of-way requirements of these regulations as determined by the
Town Engineer.
      13.   The profile grade of streets with curb and gutter shall not be less
than one-half of one percent.
      14.   Minimum street design standards shall be as follows:
 
                            Maximum                           Minimum Angle
Street         Design Speed Percent Minimum K   Minimum K Sag for
Classification              Grade   Crest Curve Curve         Intersecting
                                                              Road
Major          50           7%      44          64            60 degrees
Collector
Minor          30           7%      19          37            60 degrees
Collector
Local          30           7%      19          37            60 degrees
 
   15.   Any requested variations from the minimum street design standards
shall be reviewed by the Town Engineer. The Town Engineer shall make a written
recommendation to the Town Council regarding the requested variation. The Town
Council shall make the final decision on design variations.
   16.   Roadway access for Major and Minor Collectors shall be limited as
follows (spacing in feet):
 
Access Type Field Residential Commercial Major
Field       220   220         330        660
Residential 220   440         660        660
Commercial  330   660         660        660
Major       660   660         660        660
 
         Field - An entrance to and/or exit from a field or unoccupied property
if the access is not used daily throughout the year. Daily use for only a few
weeks a year still qualifies as field access.
         Residential - An access providing entrance to and/or exit from
residential dwelling(s) for exclusive use and benefit of those residing
therein.
         Commercial - An entrance into and/or exit from any business,
commercial development, cultural/institutional complex, public establishment,
or any development serving 10 or more family residences.
         Major - Any access that generates more than 50 trip ends in any hour
of a typical day or is a public street or access.
   C.   Lots and Blocks.
      1.   Every lot shall front on a designated collector or local street,
subject to the following exception:
         a.   Private shared access drives accessing more than one dwelling
unit may be allowable in subdivisions containing a total of three or less
dwelling units in residential zoning districts.
      2.   No residential lot shall front on an arterial street. No access
shall be permitted directly from a residential lot to an arterial street.
      3.   Every parcel of land created by a subdivision shall comply with the
minimum lot size requirements of this code and shall be platted as part of a
subdivision. No parcel of land shall be created or left unplatted which is
either undevelopable or serves merely as a nuisance or lot remnant.
      4.   Flag Lots: In order to encourage the more efficient use of land,
flag, or L-shaped lots may be allowed as an exception (a permitted use within
the sensitive area overlay district) subject to the following conditions:
         a.   The staff portion of said lot shall front on and be contiguous to
a dedicated public street or private street. The minimum width of the staff
portion of a flag lot shall be thirty feet (30'), and the maximum length shall
be two hundred feet (200') unless otherwise approved by the planning
commission.
         b.   No building or construction, except for driveways, shall be
allowed on the staff portion of said lot unless the minimum width thereof is
the same or greater than the minimum width for a lot as allowed in the
underlying zone (excluding entrance features and streetlights).
         c.   The square footage located in the flag portion of said lot, which
shall be exclusive of the square footage located in the staff portion of said
lot, shall be the same or greater than the minimum square footage as required
in the underlying zone,
         d.   The front, side, and rear yard requirements of the flag portion
of said lots shall be the same as is required in the underlying zone.
         e.   A duplex, twin home, or any other multi-family dwelling shall not
be located on a flag lot.
         f.   All flag lots in the development shall be approved by the
planning commission.
   D.   Fire Hydrants.
      1.   Fire hydrants shall be installed in all subdivision developments
when water infrastructure is extended into subdivision.
         a.   Such fire hydrants shall be of a type, size, and number as
approved by the town planning and zoning or town council and shall comply with
DEQ regulations.
         b.   Each public street shall have at least one fire hydrant.
   E.   Public sites and open spaces.
      1.   Where a proposed park, playground, school, or other public use shown
in the general plan is located in whole or in part of a subdivision, the
planning commission may require the dedication or reservation of such area
within the subdivision when the planning commission deems such requirements to
be reasonable.
   F.   Monuments.
      1.   Monuments shall be placed at all corners of all street
intersections, at the intersections of the boundary of the subdivision with
street right-of-way lines, at angle points and points of curve in each street
and at points of change in direction of the exterior boundaries of the
subdivision.
      2.   The top of the monument shall have a metal cap set flush to identify
the location. All lot corners shall be monumented with a minimum of a No. 5
rebar 24 inches in length and metal cap.
   G.   Driveways:
      1.   Driveways exceeding 200 feet in length and/or 7% grade must be
approved by the Fire Marshall.
      2.   A turnout(s) (30 feet long by 10 feet wide minimum) shall be
required for any driveway in excess of 150 feet in length, with locations
determined by the Fire Marshall.
      3.   Driveways serving single residential dwellings shall have an
improved surface of a minimum of 12 feet wide. Driveways serving two or more
residential dwellings shall have an improved surface of at least 16 feet in
width.
   H.   Easements.
      1.   Easements shall be provided for utilities where necessary and shall
be at least ten (10) feet wide or a width determined by the Town Engineer. All
lots shall have utility easements on two sides.
   I.   Signage.
      1.   All street signage shall comply with WYDOT requirements.
   J.   Other. The Town Engineer shall have the authority to determine any
design standard not addressed in this chapter.
(Ord. 373, - -2022)
CHAPTER 9: RECAPTURE FEE ORDINANCE
Section
   11-9-1: Title
   11-9-2: Policy Adopted
   11-9-3: Recapture Agreement
   11-9-4: Recapture Fee List
   11-9-5: Payment of Fee
   11-9-6: Collection of Funds
   11-9-7: Town Control of Utilities
11-9-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the Recapture Fee Ordinance.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-2: POLICY ADOPTED:
The Town of Thayne requires developers to make public works improvements
necessary for their development. Whenever such public works improvements may
benefit the owners of adjacent parcels, developers shall be entitled to
recapture a portion of the costs of such public works improvements as provided
herein.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-3: RECAPTURE AGREEMENT:
   A.   Agreement With Developer: Whenever the developer of a parcel shall be
required to install sewers or other utilities which may benefit properties not
owned by the developer, the Town of Thayne board may enter into a recapture
agreement requiring reasonable reimburse to the developer for his expenditures.
   B.   Terms Of Agreement: Each recapture agreement entered into under the
provisions of this chapter shall be negotiated by the Town of Thayne without
consideration for the existence or terms of any other such recapture
agreements, and shall contain the following provisions:
      1.   No recapture agreement shall extend for a term beyond ten (10) years
from its date.
      2.   The amount to be recaptured from each parcel shall either be set
forth specifically, or shall be determined by a precise formula which can be
used to calculate the specific sum to be recaptured.
      3.   Each parcel required to pay a recapture fee shall be specifically
identified.
      4.   The recapture agreement shall contain a finding that the amount to
be recaptured does not exceed the benefits accruing to the property required to
pay the recapture funds; and that the total amount recaptured is not greater
than the cost of providing the estimated benefits to property not owned by the
developer.
      5.   Reimbursement to the developer would be one hundred percent (100%)
of the pro rata share during the first five (5) years following construction of
the improvements; cost would then be depreciated ten percent (10%) per year
thereafter.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-4:RECAPTURE FEE LIST:
   A.   Preparation by Town of Thayne/Town Engineer: Whenever the Town of
Thayne has entered into a recapture agreement with a developer, the Town of
Thayne shall:
      1.   Within thirty (30) days, determine from the terms of the agreement
the amount of funds to be collected from each parcel of land benefited,
(hereinafter the “recapture fee”); and
      2.   Prepare an official “recapture fee list” of the said parcels setting
forth the recapture fees for each parcel.
   B.   List Submitted To Developer: The recapture fee list shall be submitted
to the developer and to the Thayne Town Council at its next regular meeting for
approval; and after being approved by the Town Council, shall be recorded by
the town clerk in the office of the recorder of deeds of Lincoln County along
with a copy of the recapture agreement.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-5: PAYMENT OF FEE:
Whenever application is made to subdivide, or for a permit to install or
construct any buildings or improvements or connect any utilities upon any
parcel listed in any recapture fee list, in addition to all other costs, fees
or requirements provided by ordinance, the applicant shall pay to the Town of
Thayne the amount set forth in the recapture fee list before the application
shall be processed.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-6: COLLECTION OF FUNDS:
Whenever any funds are collected by the Town of Thayne as provided in any
recapture agreement list, within thirty (30) days thereafter the funds shall be
forwarded to the developer, after deducting therefrom any funds which might
then be due or owing from the developer to the town.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
11-9-7:VILLAGE CONTROL OF UTILITIES:
Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, the town shall have
sole ownership and control of all and any portions of the sewer systems, water
lines, roadways, or other utilities which are constructed pursuant to any
recapture agreement.
(Ord. 374, - -2022)
TITLE 12: ANNEXATIONS
ANNEXATION; DETERMINATION OF BOUNDARIES; ADDITION AND EXCLUSION OF LAND   1
CHAPTER 1: ANNEXATION; DETERMINATION OF BOUNDARIES; ADDITION AND EXCLUSION OF
LAND
Section

12-1-2: Annexing Territories; Findings Required; When Contiguity Not Deemed
Affected; Annexation Report

12-1-4: Annexing Territories; Initiation Of Proceedings; By Governing Bodies;

12-1-6: Annexing Territories; Annexation Ordinance; Objections; Exception;

12-1-18: Annexing Contiguous Towns; Annexation Ordinance; Filing
